The Sufi Spiritual Lineage
Records the scholar's Sufi chain back to the Tabi'un.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of the Sufi chain (silsila) that connects the scholar to the early generations of Muslims.

Core Idea
The scholar's spiritual authority is validated through an unbroken chain of Sufi masters back to the Tabi'un.

This lesson records the scholar's Sufi lineage as noted by 'Abd al-Ghafir. Chains of transmission (sanad) are crucial in Islamic scholarship, and this one traces back to Dawud al-Ta'i, who met the Tabi'un. Pay attention to the named figures and the value placed on such chains.

Guided Path
1
Read the chain passage
Read the Arabic passage listing the Sufi chain. Then read the translation to follow the names in order.
The chain is presented as a sequence of 'took from' statements.
2
Identify each link in the chain
List each master in order from the scholar back to Dawud al-Ta'i. Note how many generations are involved.
There are eight named individuals before the Tabi'un are mentioned.
3
Understand the function of the chain
Reflect on why the biographer included this lineage. It authenticates the scholar's spiritual path (tariqa) and connects him to the early Sufi tradition.
The chain ends with Dawud al-Ta'i, who met the Tabi'un, giving it a direct link to the first generations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولقد قرات فصلا ذكره على بن الحسن فى دمية القصر وهو أن قال الإمام زين الإسلام أبو القسم جامع لانواع المحاسن تنقاد له صعابها ذلل المراسن ولو قرع الصخر بسوط تحذيره لذاب ولو ربط إبليس فى مجلس تذكيره لتاب، وله فصل الخطاب فى فضل المنطق المستطاب ماهر فى التكلم على مذهب الأشعرى، خارج في إحاطته بالعلوم عن الحد البشرى كلماته للمستفيدين فزائد وفوائد، وعتبات منبره للعارفين وسائدوله شعر يتتوج به رؤوس معاليه إذا ختمت به أذناب أماليه قال عبد الغافر وقد أخذ طريق التصوف من الاستاذ أبي علي الدقاق وأخذها أبو على عن أبي القسم النصر اباذي والنصراباذى عن الشبلي والشبلى عن الجنيد والجنيد عن السري السقطي والسرى عن معروف الكرخى ومعروف عن داود الطائي وداود لقى التابعين هكذا كان يذكر إسناد طريقته.
And I have read a chapter mentioned by Ali ibn al-Hasan in Dumyat al-Qasr, in which he said: 'The Imam, the Ornament of Islam, Abu al-Qasim, is a collector of all kinds of virtues; their difficulties submit to him, their obstacles are easy. If one were to strike a rock with the whip of his warning, it would melt; and if Iblis were tied in his reminding assembly, he would repent. He has the decisive speech concerning the excellence of the beloved logic; he is skilled in speaking upon the Ash'ari school; in his encompassing of sciences he exceeds the human limit. His words for students are increasing advantages, and the thresholds of his pulpit for the knowers are cushions. He has poetry that adorns the heights of his high stations when the ends of his dictations are concluded with it.' 'Abd al-Ghafir said: 'He took the path of tasawwuf from the master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq; Abu Ali took it from Abu al-Qasim al-Nasrabadhi; al-Nasrabadhi from al-Shibli; al-Shibli from al-Junayd; al-Junayd from al-Sari al-Saqati; al-Sari from Ma'ruf al-Karkhi; Ma'ruf from Dawud al-Ta'i; and Dawud met the Tabi'un.' Thus he used to mention the chain of his path.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage contains two parts. First, a quotation from Ali ibn al-Hasan's book 'Dumyat al-Qasr', which extols the scholar in highly elevated language, emphasizing his mastery of the Ash'ari school, his vast knowledge, and the power of his preaching. The quote also notes his poetry. Second, 'Abd al-Ghafir records the scholar's Sufi chain (silsila), showing his spiritual lineage through a series of famous early Sufis back to Dawud al-Ta'i, who met the Tabi'un (the generation after the Prophet's Companions). This validates his authority in tasawwuf.

Key Terms
طريق التصوف
أبو علي الدقاق
الشبلي
الجنيد
داود الطائي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Sufi chain is just a list of names with no practical significance.
Correction: In Islamic tradition, chains of transmission (sanad) are vital for preserving teachings and providing legitimacy. This chain authenticates the scholar's Sufi path and connects him to the early generations of Muslims.

Checkpoint
Through whom did the scholar's Sufi chain trace back to the Tabi'un?
A) Al-Shibli
B) Al-Junayd
C) Dawud al-Ta'i
D) Ma'ruf al-Karkhi

Key Takeaway
The scholar's Sufi lineage connects him through seven masters to Dawud al-Ta'i, who met the Tabi'un, thereby grounding his spiritual authority in the early Muslim community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This chain ends with a man who met those who saw the Companions. Do you know who taught the person who taught you about Islam? How far back can you trace your own learning, and does that lack of connection trouble you?
?
The scholar publicly cited his silsila to establish his spiritual credentials. If your own faith were traced through a chain of teachers, would that chain hold up? Whom would you credit as your reliable link to the Prophet?
?
Dawud al-Ta'i met the Tabi'un, but you live centuries later. Does that distance make the chain feel weaker or more precious to you? What are you doing to ensure that the knowledge you pass on to others is as trustworthy as the line you received?

Persecution and Exile of a Scholar
Narrates the scholar's persecution due to sectarian conflict and his journey to Baghdad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical circumstances of a scholar's trial due to sectarian fanaticism and his response in seeking refuge with the caliph.

Core Idea
Sectarian envy drove a scholar from his home, but the caliph's acceptance restored honor.

This passage recounts a painful episode in Islamic scholarship: a respected scholar was targeted by sectarian bigots and slandered until his teaching circles were shut down. Forced to leave his homeland, he journeyed to Baghdad and sought the protection of the Abbasid Caliph, who received him with honor. This story illustrates both the dangers of factionalism and the value of just leadership.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the key terms like 'trial' (محنة) and 'fanaticism' (تعصب). The passage is a single narrative paragraph.
Pay attention to the dates: 440-455 AH.
2
Identify the causes of persecution
The text mentions 'fanaticism between the two groups', 'inclination of governors to whims', and 'slandering by leaders and judges'. These are the causes.
Envy (حسد) is also cited as a motive.
3
Trace the consequences
The persecution led to 'cessation of gatherings', 'dispersal of companions', and the scholar's forced departure from his homeland. He then traveled to Baghdad.
4
Reflect on the resolution
The Caliph al-Qa'im bi-Amr Allah accepted him and held a gathering in his residence. This shows a positive outcome despite hardship.
The scholar found safety and honor in Baghdad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن جملة أحواله ما خص به من المحنة في الدين والاعتقاد وظهو التعصب بين الفريقين فى عشر سنه أربعين إلى خمس وخمسين وأربعمائة وميل بعض الولاة إلى الاهواء وسعى بعض الرؤساء والقضاة إليه بالتخليط حتى أدى ذلك إلى رفع المجالس وتفرق شمل الأصحاب وكان هو المقصود من بينهم حسداً حتى اضطرته الحال إلى مفارقة الأوطان وامتد في أثناء ذلك إلى بغداد وورد على أمير المؤمنين القائم بأمر الله، ولقى فيها قبولا وعقد له المجلس في منازله المختصة به وكان.
And among his circumstances was that which was particularly his of the trial in religion and belief, and the appearance of fanaticism between the two groups in the decade of [the years] 440 to 455 AH, and the inclination of some governors to whims, and the slandering of some leaders and judges against him with allegations of confusion, until that led to the cessation of gatherings and the dispersal of the companions. He was the intended target among them out of envy, so necessity forced him to leave his homeland. He extended during that to Baghdad and arrived before the Commander of the Faithful, al-Qa'im bi-Amr Allah. He met with acceptance there, and a gathering was held for him in his private residence.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage describes the scholar's persecution. Between the years 440 and 455 AH (c. 1048-1063 CE), sectarian fanaticism (likely between Ash'aris and Hanbalis or other groups) intensified. Some governors and judges were biased and slandered him, leading to the disruption of his teaching circles and the dispersal of his followers. He was singled out due to envy. As a result, he was forced to leave his home region. He traveled to Baghdad and sought the audience of the Abbasid Caliph al-Qa'im bi-Amr Allah, who received him honorably and allowed him to hold gatherings in his residence.

Key Terms
المحنة
التعصب
القائم بأمر الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The scholar's trial was due to his own wrongdoing or heretical views.
Correction: The text clearly states that he was targeted out of envy (حسد) and slandered by biased individuals, not because of any fault in his belief or conduct.

Checkpoint
Why was the scholar forced to leave his homeland?
A) He was accused of heresy
B) Sectarian fanaticism and slander
C) He wanted to perform Hajj
D) He was appointed as a judge elsewhere

Key Takeaway
Persecution can arise from envy and sectarianism, but seeking refuge with just authority can lead to honor and safety.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been falsely accused or mistreated because of someone's envy or sectarian bias? How did you respond, and can you see yourself turning to a just authority as the scholar did instead of seeking revenge?
?
When you witness division among Muslims today, do you recognize the role of personal whims and envy as this passage highlights? What specific step can you take to avoid being a source of such division?
?
Would you be willing to leave your home and comfort if necessity forced you for the sake of your beliefs? Are you prepared to trust that Allah will provide refuge and honor as He did for this scholar through a just ruler?

Al-Qushayri's Scholarly Excellence and Unique Talents
Description of al-Qushayri's comprehensive knowledge and dictation sessions with a laudatory quote

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth of Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri's knowledge and his unique abilities in hadith, horsemanship, dictation, and poetry.

Core Idea
Al-Qushayri was a master of both exoteric sciences and spiritual allusions.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari presents a vivid portrait of Imam al-Qushayri's multifaceted genius. From his mastery of hadith and horsemanship to his elegant poetry and dictation sessions, we see a scholar who combined outward learning with inward depth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing to analyze. Then read the translation to get a sense of the narrative flow.
Notice the shift from describing his scholarly attainments to the praise from Damyat al-Qasr.
2
Identify the areas of expertise
List the different subjects al-Qushayri mastered: hadith, horsemanship, weapons, dictation, poetry, and the Ash'ari school. How do these reflect both outward and inward knowledge?
3
Examine the quote from Damyat al-Qasr
Why does the biographer include this quote? What does it say about his influence on listeners?
The imagery of melting rock and converting Iblis emphasizes his persuasive power.
4
Reflect on his unique style
Consider his method of dictation: combining hadith with poetry and allusions. How does this reflect his integration of multiple disciplines?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحديث ببغداد والحجاز من مشايخ عصره، وكان في علم الفروسية واستعمال السلاح وما يتعلق به من أفراد العصر وله في ذلك الفن دقائق وعلوم أنفرد بها، وأما المجالس في التذكير والقعود فيما بين المريدين. وأسئلتهم عن الوقايع وخوضه في الأجوبة وجريان الأحوال العجيبة فكلها منه واليه، أجمع أهل العصر على أنه عديم النظير فيها غير مشارك في أساليب الكلام على المسائل، وتطيب القلوب والاشارات اللطيفة المستنبطة من الآيات والأخبار من كلام المشايخ والرموز الدقيقة وتصانيفه فيها المشهورة، إلى غير ذلك من نظم الأشعار اللطيفة على لسان الطريقة ولقد عقد لنفسه مجلس الاملاء في الحديث سنة سبع وثلاثين وأربعمائة فكان يملي إلى خمس وستين يذنب أماليه بأبياته وربما يتكلم على الحديث باشاراته ولطائفه وله في الكتابة طريقة أنيقة رشيقة تبنى على النظم، ولقد قرأت فصلا ذكره علي بن الحسن في (دمية القصر) وهو أن قال الإمام زين الإسلام أبو القاسم جامع لانواع المحاسن تنقاد له صعابها ذلل المراسن ولو قرع الصخر بسوط تحذيره لذاب ولو ربط إبليس في مجلس تذكيره لتاب، وله فصل الخطاب في فضل المنطق المستطاب ماهر في التكلم على مذهب الأشعري، خارج في إحاطته بالعلوم عن الحد البشري كلماته للمستفيدين فرائد وفوائد، وعتبات منبره للعارفين وسائد. وله شعر يتوجه به رؤوس معاليه إذا ختمت به أذناب أماليه، قال عبد الغافر وقد أخذ طريق التصوف من الاستاذ أبي علي الدقاق وأخذها أبو علي عن أبي القاسم النصراباذي والنصراباذي عن الشبلي والشبلي عن الجنيد والجنيد عن السري السقطي والسري عن معروف الكرخي ومعروف عن داود الطائي وداود لقي التابعين هكذا كان يذكر إسناد طريقته، ومن جملة أحواله ما خص به من المحنة في الدين والاعتقاد وظهور التعصب بين الفريقين في عشر سنه أربعين إلى خمس وخمسين وأربعمائة وميل بعض الولاة إلى الاهواء وسعي بعض الرؤساء والقضاة إليه بالتخليط حتى أدى ذلك إلى رفع المجالس وتفرق شمل الأصحاب وكان هو المقصود من بينهم حسدا حتى اضطرته الحال إلى مفارقة الأوطان وامتد في أثناء ذلك إلى بغداد وورد على أمير المؤمنين القائم بأمر الله، ولقي فيها قبولا وعقد له المجلس في منازله المختصة به وكان ذلك بمحضر ومرأى منه، ووقع كلامه من مجلسه الموقع وخرج الأمر باعزازه وإكرامه وعاد إلى نيسابور وكان يختلف منها إلى طوس بأهله وبعض أولاده، حتى طلع صبح النوبة المباركة دولة السلطان البارسلان سنة خمس وخمسين وأربعمائة، فبقي عشر سنين في آخر عمره مرفوعا محترما مطاعا معظما وأكثر صفوه في آخر أيامه التي شاهدناه فيها أخيرا إلى أن يقرأ عليه كتبه والأحاديث المسموعة له، وما يؤول إلى نصرة المذهب بلغ المنتمون إليه آلافا ملؤا بذكره وتصانيفه أطرافا، ومن نثره الكرم أطال الله بقاء الشيخ يهدي المتوسم إلى صاحبه ويقضي للمؤمل بنجح مطالبه، وأنى أجلت صواعد قصدي في كل قطر أشيم برق الحرية وأعملت قواصد فكري في كل نحو أستنشق نسيم الفتوة فما فاح إلا من بابه نشره وما لاح إلا من جنابه بشره فتعرفت إليه بأني ممن هداه إلى وده بقاء عهده وحداه على قصده ضيا مجده وأرجوانه، إذا عجم عود ولائي استصلبه وإذا قيد قلبي بإحسانه ما سيبه، والله عز وجل يديم تمكينه ويحرس عن الغير نعمته ودينه بمنه أن وجد الشيخ في مجلس العميد فراغا وللمنطق مساغا طالعه بأن فلانا إلى الباب متردد، وباقامة رسم الزيارة مستسعد وليس يشكو تحمله خجلة الحجاب ولكنه يشكو تجمله بحضور الباب والسلام، توفي صبيحة يوم الأحد قبل طلوع الشمس السادس عشر من شهر ربيع الآخر سنة خمس وستين وأربعمائة ودفن في المدرسة بجنب الأستاذ أبي علي الدقاق
Hadith in Baghdad and the Hijaz from the scholars of his era. He was in the science of horsemanship and the use of weapons and what pertains to it among the unique individuals of the age, and for him in that art there are subtleties and sciences he alone possessed. As for the assemblies of reminding and sitting among the disciples, and their questions about events, and his sinking into answers, and the flow of wondrous states, all of it proceeds from him and returns to him. The people of the era agreed that he was without equal in this, not sharing in the styles of speech on issues, and pleasing hearts, and the delicate allusions derived from the verses and reports from the speech of the shaykhs, and the precise symbols, and his famous writings in that. And besides that, the composition of delicate poems in the language of the Path. And indeed he held a dictation session in hadith in the year 437 AH, and he would dictate until [age] 65, making his dictations with his poems, and perhaps he would speak on the hadith with his allusions and subtleties. And in writing he had an elegant, graceful style built on verse. And I read a chapter mentioned by Ali ibn al-Hasan in (Damyat al-Qasr) that he said: The Imam Zayn al-Islam Abu al-Qasim is a collector of all types of beauties; their difficulties submit to him, docile in reins. If he were to strike a rock with the whip of his warning, it would melt. If he were to bind Iblis in his assembly of reminding, he would repent. He has decisive speech on the virtue of excellent logic, an expert in speaking on the Ash'ari school, beyond the human limit in his encompassing of sciences. His words are benefits and advantages for those who seek benefit, and the thresholds of his pulpit are pillows for the knowers. He has poetry that crowns the heads of his highnesses when the tails of his dictations are concluded with it. Abd al-Ghafir said: He took the path of tasawwuf from the master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, and Abu Ali took it from Abu al-Qasim al-Nasrabadhi, and al-Nasrabadhi from al-Shibli, and al-Shibli from al-Junayd, and al-Junayd from al-Sari al-Saqati, and al-Sari from Ma'ruf al-Karkhi, and Ma'ruf from Dawud al-Ta'i, and Dawud met the Successors. Thus he would mention the chain of his path. And among his circumstances was what was specially decreed for him of tribulation in religion and belief, and the appearance of partisanship between the two groups in the decade of the years 440 to 455 AH, and the inclination of some governors to passions, and the striving of some chiefs and judges against him with confusion, until that led to the raising of assemblies and the dispersal of the companions, and he was the target among them out of envy, until circumstances forced him to leave his homelands. And during that he extended to Baghdad and came before the Commander of the Faithful al-Qa'im bi-Amr Allah, and he received acceptance there, and assemblies were held for him in his private residences, and that was in his presence and sight. And his speech from his assembly had effect, and the command went out to honor and respect him, and he returned to Nishapur, and he would travel from there to Tus with his family and some of his children, until the morning of the blessed turn appeared, the state of Sultan Alp Arslan in the year 455 AH. So he remained ten years at the end of his life, elevated, respected, obeyed, glorified, and most of his leisure in his last days in which we saw him finally was for reading his books and the hadith he had heard, and what would lead to the support of the school. Those affiliated with it reached thousands, filling regions with his mention and his writings. And from his generous prose: 'May God prolong the life of the shaykh. He guides the spectator to his companion and fulfills for the hopeful the success of his goals. I have directed the peaks of my intention in every region to see the lightning of freedom, and I have employed the intentions of my thought in every direction to inhale the breeze of chivalry. It wafted only from his door, and shone only from his countenance. So I recognized him by that I am among those whom the endurance of his covenant guided to his love, and the light of his glory urged towards his intent. If the wood of my loyalty is tested, he finds it solid; if my heart is fettered by his generosity, nothing releases it. May God Almighty perpetuate his authority and guard his blessing and his religion from others, by His grace. When the shaykh found in the assembly of the 'amid a respite and for logic a passage, he perused that so-and-so is frequenting the door, and is blessed by maintaining the rite of visitation. He does not complain of the burden of the embarrassment of the veil, but complains of his adornment by attending the door and the greeting.' He died on the morning of Sunday, before sunrise, the 16th of Rabi' al-Akhir, 465 AH, and was buried in the school next to the master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a continuous biographical account of Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri (Zayn al-Islam), a leading Ash'ari theologian and Sufi master. It follows the author's sequence: first, it describes his comprehensive knowledge—including hadith, horsemanship, and the art of weapons—and his unique ability to address disciples' questions with subtle allusions and poetry. Next, it highlights his dictation sessions and his elegant writing style, then quotes a praise from Ali ibn al-Hasan's 'Damyat al-Qasr' extolling his rhetorical power and his mastery of the Ash'ari school. The biography then traces his Sufi lineage through a golden chain back to the Successors, emphasizing his spiritual authority. It proceeds to narrate the fitna (persecution) he faced around 440-455 AH due to sectarian partisanship, which forced him to flee to Baghdad, where he was honored by the caliph. After returning to Nishapur, he later enjoyed a decade of honor under Sultan Alp Arslan until his death in 465 AH. The passage concludes with a sample of his elegant prose and details of his death and burial beside Abu Ali al-Daqqaq. The commentary follows the author's narrative order, explaining each element—from his scholarly attainments, to his spiritual lineage, to his trials and final years—as a unified portrait of a multifaceted saint-scholar.

Key Terms
زين الإسلام
أبو القاسم
مذهب الأشعري
دمية القصر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think al-Qushayri was solely a Sufi mystic with little formal learning.
Correction: This passage shows he was also a master of hadith, horsemanship, weapons, and the Ash'ari school, demonstrating a synthesis of outward and inward sciences.

Checkpoint
In which year did Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri hold his first dictation (imla') session?
A) 400 AH
B) 437 AH
C) 455 AH
D) 465 AH

Key Takeaway
Al-Qushayri was a polymath who combined exoteric knowledge, spiritual subtlety, and poetic elegance in a way that his contemporaries considered unparalleled.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Qushayri combined deep formal learning with spiritual subtlety. In your own life, do you prioritize one over the other? What would it take for you to seek both with the same intensity starting today?
?
The passage says his words were 'benefits and advantages for those who seek benefit.' Are you truly seeking benefit from what you learn, or are you just accumulating information? What specific change will you make today to become a seeker of benefit?
?
He held dictation sessions until age 65. What is your commitment to lifelong learning? Are you making excuses for your own stagnation, or are you actively pursuing growth in knowledge and character? What one step will you take this week to emulate his dedication?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner

Al-Qushayri's Sufi Lineage and Spiritual Chain
Chain of transmission for al-Qushayri's Sufi path, from his teacher back to the Successors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the spiritual lineage of Imam al-Qushayri and the importance of this chain in establishing his authority as a Sufi master.

Core Idea
Al-Qushayri's Sufi chain links him to the great early mystics, authenticating his spiritual transmission.

This brief but significant passage traces the lineage of Imam al-Qushayri's Sufi path. By naming the chain of masters from his own teacher back to the Successors, it grounds his spiritual authority in an unbroken line of transmission.

Guided Path
1
Read the chain carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation, noting each name in the chain. Observe how each shaykh transmitted the path to the next.
The chain is an isnad for tasawwuf, similar to hadith transmission.
2
Recognize the significance of the chain
Understand that this chain connects al-Qushayri to al-Junayd and then to the Successors, giving his Sufi practice a prophetic root.
Al-Junayd is a central figure; Dawud al-Ta'i met the tabi'un.
3
Reflect on the phrase 'طريق التصوف'
Consider what 'path of tasawwuf' meant in the 5th century AH. This chain shows it was a transmitted discipline.
4
Memorize or write the chain
Try to reproduce the chain from memory. This helps internalize the spiritual lineage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحديث ببغداد والحجاز من مشايخ عصره، وكان في علم الفروسية واستعمال السلاح وما يتعلق به من أفراد العصر وله في ذلك الفن دقائق وعلوم أنفرد بها، وأما المجالس في التذكير والقعود فيما بين المريدين. وأسئلتهم عن الوقايع وخوضه في الأجوبة وجريان الأحوال العجيبة فكلها منه واليه، أجمع أهل العصر على أنه عديم النظير فيها غير مشارك في أساليب الكلام على المسائل، وتطيب القلوب والاشارات اللطيفة المستنبطة من الآيات والأخبار من كلام المشايخ والرموز الدقيقة وتصانيفه فيها المشهورة، إلى غير ذلك من نظم الأشعار اللطيفة على لسان الطريقة ولقد عقد لنفسه مجلس الاملاء في الحديث سنة سبع وثلاثين وأربعمائة فكان يملي إلى خمس وستين يذنب أماليه بأبياته وربما يتكلم على الحديث باشاراته ولطائفه وله في الكتابة طريقة أنيقة رشيقة تبنى على النظم، ولقد قرأت فصلا ذكره علي بن الحسن في (دمية القصر) وهو أن قال الإمام زين الإسلام أبو القاسم جامع لانواع المحاسن تنقاد له صعابها ذلل المراسن ولو قرع الصخر بسوط تحذيره لذاب ولو ربط إبليس في مجلس تذكيره لتاب، وله فصل الخطاب في فضل المنطق المستطاب ماهر في التكلم على مذهب الأشعري، خارج في إحاطته بالعلوم عن الحد البشري كلماته للمستفيدين فرائد وفوائد، وعتبات منبره للعارفين وسائد. وله شعر يتوجه به رؤوس معاليه إذا ختمت به أذناب أماليه، قال عبد الغافر وقد أخذ طريق التصوف من الاستاذ أبي علي الدقاق وأخذها أبو علي عن أبي القاسم النصراباذي والنصراباذي عن الشبلي والشبلي عن الجنيد والجنيد عن السري السقطي والسري عن معروف الكرخي ومعروف عن داود الطائي وداود لقي التابعين هكذا كان يذكر إسناد طريقته، ومن جملة أحواله ما خص به من المحنة في الدين والاعتقاد وظهور التعصب بين الفريقين في عشر سنه أربعين إلى خمس وخمسين وأربعمائة وميل بعض الولاة إلى الاهواء وسعي بعض الرؤساء والقضاة إليه بالتخليط حتى أدى ذلك إلى رفع المجالس وتفرق شمل الأصحاب وكان هو المقصود من بينهم حسدا حتى اضطرته الحال إلى مفارقة الأوطان وامتد في أثناء ذلك إلى بغداد وورد على أمير المؤمنين القائم بأمر الله، ولقي فيها قبولا وعقد له المجلس في منازله المختصة به وكان ذلك بمحضر ومرأى منه، ووقع كلامه من مجلسه الموقع وخرج الأمر باعزازه وإكرامه وعاد إلى نيسابور وكان يختلف منها إلى طوس بأهله وبعض أولاده، حتى طلع صبح النوبة المباركة دولة السلطان البارسلان سنة خمس وخمسين وأربعمائة، فبقي عشر سنين في آخر عمره مرفوعا محترما مطاعا معظما وأكثر صفوه في آخر أيامه التي شاهدناه فيها أخيرا إلى أن يقرأ عليه كتبه والأحاديث المسموعة له، وما يؤول إلى نصرة المذهب بلغ المنتمون إليه آلافا ملؤا بذكره وتصانيفه أطرافا، ومن نثره الكرم أطال الله بقاء الشيخ يهدي المتوسم إلى صاحبه ويقضي للمؤمل بنجح مطالبه، وأنى أجلت صواعد قصدي في كل قطر أشيم برق الحرية وأعملت قواصد فكري في كل نحو أستنشق نسيم الفتوة فما فاح إلا من بابه نشره وما لاح إلا من جنابه بشره فتعرفت إليه بأني ممن هداه إلى وده بقاء عهده وحداه على قصده ضيا مجده وأرجوانه، إذا عجم عود ولائي استصلبه وإذا قيد قلبي بإحسانه ما سيبه، والله عز وجل يديم تمكينه ويحرس عن الغير نعمته ودينه بمنه أن وجد الشيخ في مجلس العميد فراغا وللمنطق مساغا طالعه بأن فلانا إلى الباب متردد، وباقامة رسم الزيارة مستسعد وليس يشكو تحمله خجلة الحجاب ولكنه يشكو تجمله بحضور الباب والسلام، توفي صبيحة يوم الأحد قبل طلوع الشمس السادس عشر من شهر ربيع الآخر سنة خمس وستين وأربعمائة ودفن في المدرسة بجنب الأستاذ أبي علي الدقاق
Hadith in Baghdad and the Hijaz from the scholars of his era. He was in the science of horsemanship and the use of weapons and what pertains to it among the unique individuals of the age, and for him in that art there are subtleties and sciences he alone possessed. As for the assemblies of reminding and sitting among the disciples, and their questions about events, and his sinking into answers, and the flow of wondrous states, all of it proceeds from him and returns to him. The people of the era agreed that he was without equal in this, not sharing in the styles of speech on issues, and pleasing hearts, and the delicate allusions derived from the verses and reports from the speech of the shaykhs, and the precise symbols, and his famous writings in that. And besides that, the composition of delicate poems in the language of the Path. And indeed he held a dictation session in hadith in the year 437 AH, and he would dictate until [age] 65, making his dictations with his poems, and perhaps he would speak on the hadith with his allusions and subtleties. And in writing he had an elegant, graceful style built on verse. And I read a chapter mentioned by Ali ibn al-Hasan in (Damyat al-Qasr) that he said: The Imam Zayn al-Islam Abu al-Qasim is a collector of all types of beauties; their difficulties submit to him, docile in reins. If he were to strike a rock with the whip of his warning, it would melt. If he were to bind Iblis in his assembly of reminding, he would repent. He has decisive speech on the virtue of excellent logic, an expert in speaking on the Ash'ari school, beyond the human limit in his encompassing of sciences. His words are benefits and advantages for those who seek benefit, and the thresholds of his pulpit are pillows for the knowers. He has poetry that crowns the heads of his highnesses when the tails of his dictations are concluded with it. Abd al-Ghafir said: He took the path of tasawwuf from the master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, and Abu Ali took it from Abu al-Qasim al-Nasrabadhi, and al-Nasrabadhi from al-Shibli, and al-Shibli from al-Junayd, and al-Junayd from al-Sari al-Saqati, and al-Sari from Ma'ruf al-Karkhi, and Ma'ruf from Dawud al-Ta'i, and Dawud met the Successors. Thus he would mention the chain of his path. And among his circumstances was what was specially decreed for him of tribulation in religion and belief, and the appearance of partisanship between the two groups in the decade of the years 440 to 455 AH, and the inclination of some governors to passions, and the striving of some chiefs and judges against him with confusion, until that led to the raising of assemblies and the dispersal of the companions, and he was the target among them out of envy, until circumstances forced him to leave his homelands. And during that he extended to Baghdad and came before the Commander of the Faithful al-Qa'im bi-Amr Allah, and he received acceptance there, and assemblies were held for him in his private residences, and that was in his presence and sight. And his speech from his assembly had effect, and the command went out to honor and respect him, and he returned to Nishapur, and he would travel from there to Tus with his family and some of his children, until the morning of the blessed turn appeared, the state of Sultan Alp Arslan in the year 455 AH. So he remained ten years at the end of his life, elevated, respected, obeyed, glorified, and most of his leisure in his last days in which we saw him finally was for reading his books and the hadith he had heard, and what would lead to the support of the school. Those affiliated with it reached thousands, filling regions with his mention and his writings. And from his generous prose: 'May God prolong the life of the shaykh. He guides the spectator to his companion and fulfills for the hopeful the success of his goals. I have directed the peaks of my intention in every region to see the lightning of freedom, and I have employed the intentions of my thought in every direction to inhale the breeze of chivalry. It wafted only from his door, and shone only from his countenance. So I recognized him by that I am among those whom the endurance of his covenant guided to his love, and the light of his glory urged towards his intent. If the wood of my loyalty is tested, he finds it solid; if my heart is fettered by his generosity, nothing releases it. May God Almighty perpetuate his authority and guard his blessing and his religion from others, by His grace. When the shaykh found in the assembly of the 'amid a respite and for logic a passage, he perused that so-and-so is frequenting the door, and is blessed by maintaining the rite of visitation. He does not complain of the burden of the embarrassment of the veil, but complains of his adornment by attending the door and the greeting.' He died on the morning of Sunday, before sunrise, the 16th of Rabi' al-Akhir, 465 AH, and was buried in the school next to the master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a continuous biographical account of Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri (Zayn al-Islam), a leading Ash'ari theologian and Sufi master. It follows the author's sequence: first, it describes his comprehensive knowledge—including hadith, horsemanship, and the art of weapons—and his unique ability to address disciples' questions with subtle allusions and poetry. Next, it highlights his dictation sessions and his elegant writing style, then quotes a praise from Ali ibn al-Hasan's 'Damyat al-Qasr' extolling his rhetorical power and his mastery of the Ash'ari school. The biography then traces his Sufi lineage through a golden chain back to the Successors, emphasizing his spiritual authority. It proceeds to narrate the fitna (persecution) he faced around 440-455 AH due to sectarian partisanship, which forced him to flee to Baghdad, where he was honored by the caliph. After returning to Nishapur, he later enjoyed a decade of honor under Sultan Alp Arslan until his death in 465 AH. The passage concludes with a sample of his elegant prose and details of his death and burial beside Abu Ali al-Daqqaq. The commentary follows the author's narrative order, explaining each element—from his scholarly attainments, to his spiritual lineage, to his trials and final years—as a unified portrait of a multifaceted saint-scholar.

Key Terms
زين الإسلام
أبو القاسم
طريق التصوف
أبو علي الدقاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Sufi paths are later innovations without a chain back to the Prophet.
Correction: This chain shows that al-Qushayri's Sufi lineage goes back to the Successors, demonstrating its early roots.

Checkpoint
According to the chain, which figure met the Successors (tabi'un)?
A) Abu Ali al-Daqqaq
B) Dawud al-Ta'i
C) Al-Junayd
D) Ma'ruf al-Karkhi

Key Takeaway
Al-Qushayri's Sufi path is authenticated by a continuous chain of masters leading back to the early Muslim community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This chain traces spiritual knowledge back to the early generations. Who is your spiritual teacher or guide? Do you have a chain of transmission for what you believe and practice, or are you disconnected from those who came before?
?
Al-Qushayri would recite his chain publicly. If you had to recite the chain of knowledge that shapes your Islam today, could you name even one person between you and the Prophet? What would it mean to you to be able to do so?
?
The chain ends with Dawud al-Ta'i meeting the Successors—those who knew the Companions. Do you feel any personal responsibility to preserve and pass on authentic Islamic knowledge to the next generation? How will you ensure the chain does not break with you?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
5 min
Persecution and Final Years of al-Qushayri
Narrative of al-Qushayri's persecution, exile, return to honor, and death, with a sample of his prose

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the trials faced by al-Qushayri due to sectarian conflict, his exile to Baghdad, his return to honor, and his death.

Core Idea
Al-Qushayri endured persecution for his beliefs but ultimately found honor and left a lasting legacy.

This concluding section of the biography narrates the fitna that befell al-Qushayri, his flight to Baghdad, his rehabilitation under Sultan Alp Arslan, and his final years. It also includes a sample of his elegant prose and details of his death.

Guided Path
1
Read about the persecution
Read the passage focusing on the fitna – what caused it, who was involved, and how al-Qushayri was singled out. Note the time frame (440-455 AH).
The persecution was due to sectarian partisanship and envy.
2
Follow his journey to Baghdad
Trace al-Qushayri's exile: he went to Baghdad, met the caliph al-Qa'im, and received honor. How did the caliph receive him?
He was allowed to hold assemblies and was honored.
3
Note his return and later years
After returning to Nishapur, he enjoyed ten years of honor under Sultan Alp Arslan. What does the passage say about his activities?
He continued teaching and supporting the Ash'ari school.
4
Read the prose sample and death account
The passage includes a sample of his prose. Read it as an example of his style. Then note the exact date and place of his death and burial.
He died on Sunday, 16 Rabi' al-Akhir 465 AH, and was buried next to his teacher Abu Ali al-Daqqaq.

عود ولائي استصلبه وإذا قيد قلبي بإحسانه ما سيبه، والله عز وجل يديم تمكينه ويحرس عن الغير نعمته ودينه بمنه أن وجد الشيخ في مجلس العميد فراغا وللمنطق مساغا طالعه بأن فلانا إلى الباب متردد، وباقامة رسم الزيارة مستسعد وليس يشكو تحمله خجلة الحجاب ولكنه يشكو تجمله بحضور الباب والسلام، توفي صبيحة يوم الأحد قبل طلوع الشمس السادس عشر من شهر ربيع الآخر سنة خمس وستين وأربعمائة ودفن في المدرسة بجنب الأستاذ أبي علي الدقاق
Hadith in Baghdad and the Hijaz from the scholars of his era. He was in the science of horsemanship and the use of weapons and what pertains to it among the unique individuals of the age, and for him in that art there are subtleties and sciences he alone possessed. As for the assemblies of reminding and sitting among the disciples, and their questions about events, and his sinking into answers, and the flow of wondrous states, all of it proceeds from him and returns to him. The people of the era agreed that he was without equal in this, not sharing in the styles of speech on issues, and pleasing hearts, and the delicate allusions derived from the verses and reports from the speech of the shaykhs, and the precise symbols, and his famous writings in that. And besides that, the composition of delicate poems in the language of the Path. And indeed he held a dictation session in hadith in the year 437 AH, and he would dictate until [age] 65, making his dictations with his poems, and perhaps he would speak on the hadith with his allusions and subtleties. And in writing he had an elegant, graceful style built on verse. And I read a chapter mentioned by Ali ibn al-Hasan in (Damyat al-Qasr) that he said: The Imam Zayn al-Islam Abu al-Qasim is a collector of all types of beauties; their difficulties submit to him, docile in reins. If he were to strike a rock with the whip of his warning, it would melt. If he were to bind Iblis in his assembly of reminding, he would repent. He has decisive speech on the virtue of excellent logic, an expert in speaking on the Ash'ari school, beyond the human limit in his encompassing of sciences. His words are benefits and advantages for those who seek benefit, and the thresholds of his pulpit are pillows for the knowers. He has poetry that crowns the heads of his highnesses when the tails of his dictations are concluded with it. Abd al-Ghafir said: He took the path of tasawwuf from the master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, and Abu Ali took it from Abu al-Qasim al-Nasrabadhi, and al-Nasrabadhi from al-Shibli, and al-Shibli from al-Junayd, and al-Junayd from al-Sari al-Saqati, and al-Sari from Ma'ruf al-Karkhi, and Ma'ruf from Dawud al-Ta'i, and Dawud met the Successors. Thus he would mention the chain of his path. And among his circumstances was what was specially decreed for him of tribulation in religion and belief, and the appearance of partisanship between the two groups in the decade of the years 440 to 455 AH, and the inclination of some governors to passions, and the striving of some chiefs and judges against him with confusion, until that led to the raising of assemblies and the dispersal of the companions, and he was the target among them out of envy, until circumstances forced him to leave his homelands. And during that he extended to Baghdad and came before the Commander of the Faithful al-Qa'im bi-Amr Allah, and he received acceptance there, and assemblies were held for him in his private residences, and that was in his presence and sight. And his speech from his assembly had effect, and the command went out to honor and respect him, and he returned to Nishapur, and he would travel from there to Tus with his family and some of his children, until the morning of the blessed turn appeared, the state of Sultan Alp Arslan in the year 455 AH. So he remained ten years at the end of his life, elevated, respected, obeyed, glorified, and most of his leisure in his last days in which we saw him finally was for reading his books and the hadith he had heard, and what would lead to the support of the school. Those affiliated with it reached thousands, filling regions with his mention and his writings. And from his generous prose: 'May God prolong the life of the shaykh. He guides the spectator to his companion and fulfills for the hopeful the success of his goals. I have directed the peaks of my intention in every region to see the lightning of freedom, and I have employed the intentions of my thought in every direction to inhale the breeze of chivalry. It wafted only from his door, and shone only from his countenance. So I recognized him by that I am among those whom the endurance of his covenant guided to his love, and the light of his glory urged towards his intent. If the wood of my loyalty is tested, he finds it solid; if my heart is fettered by his generosity, nothing releases it. May God Almighty perpetuate his authority and guard his blessing and his religion from others, by His grace. When the shaykh found in the assembly of the 'amid a respite and for logic a passage, he perused that so-and-so is frequenting the door, and is blessed by maintaining the rite of visitation. He does not complain of the burden of the embarrassment of the veil, but complains of his adornment by attending the door and the greeting.' He died on the morning of Sunday, before sunrise, the 16th of Rabi' al-Akhir, 465 AH, and was buried in the school next to the master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a continuous biographical account of Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri (Zayn al-Islam), a leading Ash'ari theologian and Sufi master. It follows the author's sequence: first, it describes his comprehensive knowledge—including hadith, horsemanship, and the art of weapons—and his unique ability to address disciples' questions with subtle allusions and poetry. Next, it highlights his dictation sessions and his elegant writing style, then quotes a praise from Ali ibn al-Hasan's 'Damyat al-Qasr' extolling his rhetorical power and his mastery of the Ash'ari school. The biography then traces his Sufi lineage through a golden chain back to the Successors, emphasizing his spiritual authority. It proceeds to narrate the fitna (persecution) he faced around 440-455 AH due to sectarian partisanship, which forced him to flee to Baghdad, where he was honored by the caliph. After returning to Nishapur, he later enjoyed a decade of honor under Sultan Alp Arslan until his death in 465 AH. The passage concludes with a sample of his elegant prose and details of his death and burial beside Abu Ali al-Daqqaq. The commentary follows the author's narrative order, explaining each element—from his scholarly attainments, to his spiritual lineage, to his trials and final years—as a unified portrait of a multifaceted saint-scholar.

Key Terms
المحنة
بغداد
القائم بأمر الله
السلطان البارسلان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that al-Qushayri's life was always peaceful and honored.
Correction: This passage shows he endured severe persecution and exile, only finding stability and honor later in life.

Checkpoint
On what exact date did al-Qushayri die according to the passage?

Key Takeaway
Despite facing severe persecution and exile, al-Qushayri was ultimately honored and left a profound impact on the Ash'ari school and Sufi tradition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Qushayri was targeted out of envy and forced to leave his homeland. Which relationships or environments in your life are poisoned by envy? Are you willing to leave them behind for the sake of your faith, if necessary?
?
He was honored after years of humiliation. When you face rejection or opposition for your beliefs, do you truly trust that God will honor you in His time? Reflect on a specific trial where you struggled with patience.
?
His final years were spent teaching and supporting the school. What legacy are you building today? If your life were to end now, what would be the 'school' you leave behind—what truth or good have you championed?

Biography of Abu Ali ibn Abi Haritha al-Hamadani
Biographical notice of a Maliki-Ash'ari scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly profile of Abu Ali ibn Abi Haritha, a Maliki jurist who adhered to Ash'ari theology.

Core Idea
Ash'ari theology transcends legal schools — even Malikis were its followers.

This short biographical notice from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari introduces us to a lesser-known scholar, Abu Ali ibn Abi Haritha. The passage is significant because it demonstrates that Ash'ari theological commitments were not limited to the Shafi'i madhhab but were embraced by Maliki jurists as well. Let's examine what this notice tells us about his life and affiliations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the full lineage and the date of death.
The opening 'ومنهم' shows this is part of a list of scholars.
2
Identify the key details
Find the two schools mentioned: his legal madhhab (Maliki) and his theological school (Ash'ari). Note the contrast between his fiqh and his 'aqidah.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: why did Ibn 'Asakir include this detail? What does it teach about the spread of Ash'ari theology?
This addresses the common misconception that all Ash'aris were Shafi'is.

ومنهم أبو علي بن أبي حريصة الهمداني الدمشقى الفقيه رحمه الله ) قال لي الشيخ الأمين أبو محمد هبة الله بن أحمد الأكفاني توفى أبو على الحسين بن أحمد بن المظفر بن أحمد بن سليمان بن المتوكل بن أبى حريصة الهمداني رحمه الله يوم الثلاثاء السادس والعشرين من المحرم من سنة ست وستين وأربعمائة، وكان قد كتب الكثير وحدث باليسير وكان فقيهاً على مذهب مالك ويذهب مذهب أبي الحسن الأشعري
And among them is Abu Ali ibn Abi Haritha al-Hamadani al-Dimashqi, the jurist, may God have mercy on him. The trustworthy shaykh Abu Muhammad Hibatullah ibn Ahmad al-Akfani told me: Abu Ali al-Husayn ibn Ahmad ibn al-Muzaffar ibn Ahmad ibn Sulayman ibn al-Mutawakkil ibn Abi Haritha al-Hamadani, may God have mercy on him, died on Tuesday, the 26th of al-Muharram of the year 466 AH. He had written much and narrated a little, and he was a jurist according to the school of Malik and followed the school of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a brief biographical notice of Abu Ali ibn Abi Haritha, a Maliki jurist from Damascus. The author, Ibn 'Asakir, records his full lineage and death date, then notes that although he was a Maliki in fiqh, he adhered to the Ash'ari school of theology. This illustrates the principle that Ash'ari theology was not confined to the Shafi'i madhhab but was espoused by scholars of other legal schools as well. The passage also indicates that he wrote many works but narrated few hadith orally.

Introducing Abu al-Muzaffar al-Isfarayini in a Biographical Notice
Opening of a biographical entry on Abu al-Muzaffar al-Isfarayini

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how classical biographical dictionaries introduce a subject and the meaning of the honorific titles used in such entries.

Core Idea
A single sentence can reveal a scholar's legacy through names and titles.

Imam Ibn 'Asakir begins the biography of Abu al-Muzaffar al-Isfarayini by citing his source and listing the subject's full name and honorifics. This opening follows the conventions of medieval Islamic biographical literature, where a chain of transmission and precise identification are essential.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the use of 'كتب إلى' indicating a written transmission.
2
Identify the names and titles
The passage contains the full name of the biographer and the subject. Note the two-part name of the biographer and the full lineage of Abu al-Muzaffar, followed by his honorific titles.
The title 'الإمام الكامل' (the complete Imam) is significant.
3
Understand the source citation
The biographer, Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir al-Farsi, is cited as the source. This is a common practice in tabaqat works to show the chain of transmission.
This chain gives authority to the biographical information.
4
Reflect on the meaning of 'the complete Imam'
Consider why the title 'الإمام الكامل' (the complete Imam) might be used. This indicates that the subject was seen as a leading scholar with full mastery of his fields.
Such epithets are common in biographic entries to convey respect and status.

However, the biography is truncated at this point in the available pages, providing only the initial identification. The reader is left to continue the entry from subsequent folios of the work.

Conclusion of a Scholar's Biography: Death and Burial
Ibn Asakir concludes the biography of a prominent Ash'ari scholar detailing his final years and death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the final years and legacy of a prominent Ash'ari scholar as narrated by Ibn Asakir, including the circumstances of his death and burial.

Core Idea
A scholar's life culminates in honor, legacy, and a burial place among the righteous.

Ibn Asakir concludes his biography with a portrait of the scholar's exalted final years—ten years of reverence, teaching, and prolific influence. The passage then weaves into a poetic tribute before recording the precise date and place of death. This lesson explores how Ibn Asakir memorializes the scholar and what his account reveals about the scholarly community of the time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the timeline
Identify the sequence of events from the scholar's return to Nishapur to his death. Note the mention of Sultan Alp Arslan's reign.
The ten-year period at the end is emphasized.
2
Examine the shift to poetic prose
The passage transitions into a stylized praise describing the scholar's generosity and the author's connection to him. Notice the elaborate language.
This reflects literary conventions of biographical writing.
3
Locate the death and burial details
Find the exact date and place of burial. Note the significance of being buried next to Abu Ali al-Daqqaq.
This highlights the scholar's association with Sufi circles.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك بمحضر ومرأى منه ، وقع كلامه من مجلسه الموقع وخرج الأمر باعزازه وإكرامه وعاد إلى نيسابور وكان يختلف منها إلى طوس بأهله وبعض أولاده ، حتى طلع صبح النوبة المباركة دولة السلطان البارسلان سنة خمس وخمسين وأربعماية ، فبقى عشر سنين في آخر عمره مرفوعا محترماً مطاعاً معظماً وأكثر صفوه في آخر أيامه التي شاهدناه فيها أخيراً إلى أن يقرأ عليه كتبه والأحاديث المسموعة له ، وما يؤول إلى نصرة المذهب بلغ المنتمون إليه آلافا ملؤا بذكره وتصانيفه أطرافا ، ومن نثره الكرم أطال الله بقاء الشيخ يهدى المتوسم إلى صاحبه ويقضى للمؤمل بنجح مطالبه وأنى أجلت صواعد قصدى فى كل قطر أشيم برق الحرية وأعملت قواصد فكرى فى كل نحو أستنشق نسيم الفتوة فما فاح إلا من بابه نشره وما لاح إلا من جنابه بشره فتعرفت إليه بأنى ممن هداه إلى وده بقاء عهده وحداه على قصده ضيا مجده وأرجوانه ، إذا عجم عود ولائى استصلبه وإذا قيد قلبي بإحسانه ما سيبه ، والله عز وجل يديم تمكينه ويحرس عن الغير نعمته ودينه بمنه أن وجد الشيخ في مجلس العميد فراغا وللمنطق مساغا طالعه بأن فلانا إلى الباب متردد ، وباقامة رسم الزيارة مستسعد وليس يشكو تحمله خجلة الحجاب ولكنه يشكو تجمله بحضور الباب والسلام ، توفي صبيحة يوم الأحد قبل طلوع الشمس السادس عشر من شهر ربيع الآخر سنة خمس وستين وأربعمائة ودفن في المدرسة بجنب الأستاذ أبي على الدقاق
That was in his presence and sight, and his speech from his council took effect, and the command came out honoring and revering him, and he returned to Nishapur and used to travel from there to Tus with his family and some of his children, until the morning of the blessed turn of the state of Sultan Alp Arslan in the year 455 AH. So he remained ten years at the end of his life, elevated, respected, obeyed, and venerated, and most of his pure deeds in his last days that we witnessed recently were that his books and the hadiths heard by him were recited to him, and what pertained to supporting the madhhab; those who adhered to it reached thousands, filling regions with his mention and his writings. And from his generous prose: 'May Allah prolong the life of the Shaykh; he guides the discerning to his companion and fulfills for the hopeful his aims. And indeed I directed the peaks of my intention in every region, looking at the lightning of freedom, and I set in motion the directions of my thought in every direction, sniffing the breeze of chivalry; it wafted only from his door, its fragrance shone only from his courtyard, its good news. So I introduced myself to him as one whom the continuation of his covenant guided to his love and the radiance of his glory and its crimson drove him to his purpose. If the wood of my loyalty is tested, he finds it solid, and if my heart is bound by his kindness, he frees it. May Allah Almighty perpetuate his empowerment and protect from others His favor and His religion by His grace. He found the Shaykh in the council of the chief having leisure and logic having passage, and he informed him that so-and-so was hovering at the door, and he was blessed with establishing the ritual of visitation. He does not complain of bearing the shame of the veil but he complains of his adornment by attending the door and greeting. He died on the morning of Sunday before sunrise, the sixteenth of Rabi' al-Akhir, year 465 AH, and was buried in the school next to the master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq.'
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is the conclusion of a biography of a prominent Ash'ari scholar, likely Abd al-Karim al-Qushayri, though his name is not explicitly mentioned in this extract. Ibn Asakir describes the scholar's final years: he was highly respected and honored, returning to Nishapur and traveling to Tus. He lived through the reign of Sultan Alp Arslan, and in his last ten years he was venerated and his works were recited. The passage then shifts to a poetic prose piece praising the scholar, highlighting his generosity and his role in guiding others. It concludes with the date and place of his death: Sunday, 16 Rabi' al-Akhir 465 AH, and his burial in the school next to Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, a notable Sufi master. The commentary does not add external identification but explains the flow of the text.

Core Idea
Ibn Asakir preserves a scholar's legacy through a concise, structured biographical note.

In this passage, Ibn Asakir presents a concise biography of Abu al-Muzaffar al-Isfarayini, a prominent Shafi'i-Ash'ari scholar. The entry, transmitted via a letter from Abd al-Ghafir al-Farsi, highlights his titles (faqih, usuli, mufassir), his connection to the Seljuk vizier Nizam al-Mulk at Tus, and his death year. This example illustrates the tabaqat genre and its role in preserving scholarly heritage.

Notice the chain of transmission: Ibn Asakir cites al-Farsi.

Identify key biographical elements

Consider why such brief entries were important for preserving scholarly networks and memory.
They connect scholars across time and place.

Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi: Biography and Defense of His Ash'arism
Ibn Asakir defends al-Shirazi's Ash'arism after detailing his biography.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir defends Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi's Ash'ari affiliation by distinguishing between a specific legal disagreement and rejection of the entire creed.

Core Idea
Disagreement on one issue does not negate doctrinal allegiance.

Ibn Asakir introduces the renowned Shafi'i jurist Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, highlighting his scholarly credentials and major works. He then confronts a claim that al-Shirazi opposed Ash'ari theology based on a single statement about the command in usul al-fiqh. By examining al-Shirazi's own fatwa condemning those who consider Ash'aris innovators, Ibn Asakir conclusively demonstrates al-Shirazi's Ash'arism.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical details
Read the first part of the Arabic passage to appreciate al-Shirazi's scholarly stature: his teachers, his teaching at the Nizamiyya, and his famous books.
2
Identify the misconception
Notice the sentence that begins 'وكان يظن به بعض من لا يفهم...' which presents the claim that al-Shirazi opposed al-Ash'ari due to his statement on the command.
The statement in question is: 'وقالت الأشعرية أن الأمر لا صيغة له'
3
Follow Ibn Asakir's rebuttal
Read how Ibn Asakir explains that al-Shirazi only disagreed on this particular issue, not on the entire creed. He cites al-Shirazi's fatwa against those who oppose Ash'aris as evidence.
Key phrase: 'وذلك أوفى دليل على أنه منهم'
4
Reflect on the poem
Consider the poetic eulogy found in a manuscript, praising al-Shirazi and his work al-Tanbih. It underscores his piety and commitment to the Shari'a.
The poem is incomplete; the passage ends mid-line.

ومنهم الشيخ أبو إسحق إبراهيم بن على بن يوسف الشيرازي ثم الفيروزاباذى الفقيه الزاهد والناسك العابد ذو التصانيف الحسنة والتواليف المستحسنة، سكن بغداد وسمع الحديث بها من أبى على بن شاذان وأبى بكر البرقاني وغيرهما، وتفقه على جماعة منهم القاضي أبو الطيب الطبرى وأبو أحمد عبد الوهاب بن محمد بن عمر بن محمد بن رامين وأبو عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله بن أحمد البيضاوي وأبو القسم منصور بن عمر الكرخي البغداديون، وأبو حاتم محمود بن الحسن الطبري وأبو عبد الله محمد بن عمر الشيرازي وغيرهم درس ببغداد بالمدرسة النظامية وهو صاحب كتاب ( المهذب ) وكتاب ( التنبيه ) في المذهب و ( النكت ( في الخلاف ) واللمع ( في أصول الفقه وغير ذلك من الكتب، وكان يظن به بعض من لا يفهم أنه مخالف للأشعرى لقوله في كتابه في أصول الفقه وقالت الأشعرية أن الأمر لا صيغة له وليس ذلك لأنه لا يعتقد اعتقاده، وإنما قال ذلك لأنه خالفه فى هذه المسئلة بعينها كما خالفه غيره من الفقهاء فيها فأراد أن يبين فيها أن هذه المسئلة مما انفرد بها أبو الحسن وقد ذكرنا في كتابنا هذا عنه فتواه فيمن خالف الأشعرية واعتقد تبديعهم وذلك أوفى دليل على أنه منهم. وجدت بخط أخى أبى الحسين هبة الله بن الحسن بن هبة الله للرئيس أبي الخطاب على بن عبد الرحمن بن عيسى بن علی بن عیسی بن داود بن رحمه الله الجراح الكاتب البغدادى فى الشيخ أبي إسحق إبراهيم ابن على الشيرازي سقيًا لمن ألف التنبيه مختصرا ألفاظه الغر واستقصى معانيه أن الإمام أبا إسحق صنفه الله والدين لا للكبر والتيه رأى علوما عن الإفهام شاردة فحازها ابن على كلها فيه لازلت للشرع إبراهيم منتصرا تذود عنه أعاديه وتحـــــــــه أنشدنا أبو القسم إسماعيل بن أحمد بن السمرقندي ببغداد قال أنشدنا الشيخ الإمام أبو إسحق الشيرازي بنفسه :
And among them is the shaykh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Ali ibn Yusuf al-Shirazi, then al-Firuzabadi, the faqih, the ascetic, the devout worshipper, possessor of fine works and commendable compositions. He resided in Baghdad and heard hadith there from Abu Ali ibn Shadhan, Abu Bakr al-Barqani, and others. He studied fiqh under a group including al-Qadi Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari, Abu Ahmad Abd al-Wahhab ibn Muhammad ibn Umar ibn Muhammad ibn Ramin, Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Abd Allah ibn Ahmad al-Baydawi, Abu al-Qasim Mansur ibn Umar al-Karkhi al-Baghdadi, Abu Hatim Mahmud ibn al-Hasan al-Tabari, and Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Umar al-Shirazi, and others. He taught in Baghdad at the Nizamiyya school. He is the author of the book 'al-Muhadhdhab', 'al-Tanbih' on the madhhab, 'al-Nukat' on legal disagreement, 'al-Luma' on usul al-fiqh, and other books. Some who lack understanding suspected that he opposed al-Ash'ari because of his statement in his book on usul al-fiqh: 'The Ash'aris said that the command has no linguistic form.' That is not because he did not believe his belief; rather, he said that because he disagreed with him on this particular issue, just as other jurists disagreed with him on it. He wanted to show that this issue is one in which Abu al-Hasan was unique. And we have mentioned in this book of ours his fatwa regarding those who oppose the Ash'aris and believe in declaring them innovators, and that is the most sufficient evidence that he is from them. I found in the handwriting of my brother Abu al-Husayn Hibat Allah ibn al-Hasan ibn Hibat Allah, for al-Ra'is Abu al-Khattab Ali ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Isa ibn Ali ibn Isa ibn Dawud ibn [؟] rahimahu Allah al-Jarrah, the scribe of Baghdad, concerning the shaykh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Ali al-Shirazi: 'Rain for the one who authored al-Tanbih as an abridgment, his brilliant expressions and mastered its meanings. Indeed, Imam Abu Ishaq composed it for Allah and religion, not for pride or arrogance. He saw sciences evading minds, so Ibn Ali gathered them all in it. May you always, Ibrahim, be a supporter of the Shari'a, repelling its enemies and [؟].' Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn al-Samarqandi recited to us in Baghdad, saying: the shaykh, the imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi recited to us by himself: ...
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This is a substantial biographical entry for Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, the famous Shafi'i jurist and author of foundational texts. Ibn Asakir lists his teachers, his residence in Baghdad, his teaching at the Nizamiyya school, and his major works: al-Muhadhdhab, al-Tanbih, al-Nukat, al-Luma. Then Ibn Asakir addresses a misconception: some people thought al-Shirazi opposed Ash'ari theology because he wrote in his usul al-fiqh that 'the Ash'aris said the command has no linguistic form' (a position that seems to imply disagreement). Ibn Asakir explains that al-Shirazi only disagreed with al-Ash'ari on this specific issue, not on the entire creed. He further provides evidence that al-Shirazi was indeed an Ash'ari: his fatwa against those who oppose the Ash'aris and consider them innovators. The entry concludes with a poetic eulogy found in the handwriting of another scholar, praising al-Shirazi's work al-Tanbih, and a note that Abu Ishaq himself recited a poem (the text ends mid-sentence). This passage is important for understanding how Ibn Asakir defends the Ash'arism of certain scholars against accusations.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi opposed Ash'ari theology because he wrote that 'the Ash'aris said the command has no linguistic form.'
Correction: Ibn Asakir clarifies that al-Shirazi only disagreed on this single issue of usul al-fiqh, not on Ash'ari doctrine overall. He cites al-Shirazi's fatwa against those who consider Ash'aris innovators as clear proof of his Ash'arism.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, what evidence proves that Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi was an Ash'ari?
A) His book al-Muhadhdhab
B) His fatwa against those who oppose Ash'aris
C) His studying under Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari
D) His teaching at the Nizamiyya

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir uses a scholar's own fatwa as conclusive evidence of his doctrinal affiliation, showing that disagreement on a single issue does not negate overall allegiance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed someone's entire belief system because of a single disagreement? How does this lesson challenge your willingness to distinguish between core allegiance and peripheral differences in your own relationships with fellow Muslims?
?
Ibn Asakir used a scholar's own fatwa as decisive evidence of his doctrinal affiliation. If your life were to be judged by your own actions and rulings, would they show what you truly believe? Is there a gap between what you claim and what you practice that you need to confront today?
?
The misconception about al-Shirazi arose from ignorance ('some who lack understanding'). Are there people you have judged without understanding their full context? What step can you take this week to seek clarity before passing judgment on someone's faith or intentions?

The Virtues and Early Training of Imam al-Juwayni
Ibn Asakir describes Imam al-Juwayni's scholarly excellence and early education.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the exceptional scholarly qualities and early education of Imam al-Juwayni as described by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
Imam al-Juwayni's eloquence and scholarship were unparalleled, rooted in early training and personal effort.

This passage offers a vivid portrait of Imam al-Juwayni, celebrating his intellectual and spiritual stature. Ibn Asakir emphasizes his unmatched eloquence, deep mastery of Arabic, and rigorous scholarly formation under his father. As you read, note how the author blends hyperbolic praise with concrete details to convey his subject's greatness.

Guided Path
1
Encounter the biographical context
The passage introduces Imam al-Juwayni with a chain of transmission. Read the opening lines to understand his identity and the source of the narrative.
Notice the honorific titles like 'Imam al-Haramayn'.
2
Observe the superlative praise
Notice the series of epithets and comparisons (e.g., 'eyes have not seen his like'). Reflect on the purpose of such praise in biographical writing.
3
Examine his eloquence
The passage describes his lectures as lightning-like and his speech as unmatched. Compare the description of his oral delivery with his written works.
The phrase 'غَيْض من فَيْض' is key.
4
Trace his early training
Learn about his father's role and how al-Juwayni went beyond taqlid to engage in verification and debate.
Note the transition from taqlid to tahqiq.
5
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how this biography illustrates the ideal of combining inherited knowledge with independent inquiry.

ومنهم الإمام أبو المعالي الجويني النيسابوري رحمه الله

أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن بن أبي عبد الله بن أبي الحسين الأديب في كتابه قال : عبد الملك بن عبد الله بن يوسف الجويني أبو المعالي ابن ركن الإسلام أبي محمد إمام الحرمين فجر الإسلام ، أمام الأئمة على الإطلاق الشريعة المجمع على إمامته شرقاً وغرباً المقر بفضله السراة والحراة عجماً وعربا من لم تر العيون مثله قبله ولا ترى بعده ، رباه حجر الأمامة وحرك ساعد السعادة مهده وأرضعه لدى العلم والورع إلى أن ترعرع فيه ويفع ، من العربية وما يتعلق بها أو فرحظ ونصيب فزاد فيها على كل أديب ورزق من التوسع في العبارة وعلوها ما لم يعهد من غيره حتى أنسى ذكر سحبان ، وفاق فيها الأقران وحمل القرآن وأعجز الفصحاء اللد وجاوز الوصف والحد ، وكل من سمع خبره أو رأى أثره فإذا شاهده أقر بأن خبره يزيد كثيرا على الخبر ويبر على ما عهد من الأثر ، وكان يذكر دروساً يقع كل واحد منها في أطباق وأوراق لا يتلعثم فى كلمة ولا يحتاج إلى استدراك عشرة مراراً فيها كالبرق الخاطف بصوت مطابق كالرعد القاصف ينزف فيه المبرزون ولا يدرك شأوه المتشدقون المتعمقون ، وما يوجد منه في كتبه من العبارات البالغة كنه الفصاحة غيض من فيض ما كان على لسانه وغرفة من أمواج ما كان يعهد من بيانه ، تفقه في صباه على والده ركن الإسلام فكان يزهى بطلعه وتحصيله وجودة قريحته وكياسة غريزته ، لما يرى فيه من المخايل فخلفه فيه من بعد وفاته وأتى على جميع مصنفاته فقلبها ظهرا لبطن وتصرف فيها وخرج المسائل بعضها على بعض ودرس سنين ولم يرض فى شبابه بتقليد والده وأصحابه ، حتى أخذ في التحقيق وجد واجتهد في المذهب والخلاف ومجالس النظر ، حتى ظهرت نجابته
And among them is the Imam Abu al-Ma'ali al-Juwayni al-Naysaburi, may Allah have mercy on him. The Shaykh Abu al-Hasan ibn Abi 'Abd Allah ibn Abi al-Husayn al-Adib informed us in his book, saying: 'Abd al-Malik ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Yusuf al-Juwayni, Abu al-Ma'ali, son of Rukn al-Islam Abu Muhammad, Imam al-Haramayn, the dawn of Islam, the Imam of Imams absolutely, the Shari'a, the one unanimously recognized as imam in east and west, whose virtue is acknowledged by nobles and free men, non-Arabs and Arabs. Eyes have not seen his like before him nor will they see after him. The cradle of imamate raised him, the arm of happiness rocked his cradle, and he was nurtured in knowledge and piety until he grew up and flourished. He had a great share of Arabic and what pertains to it, surpassing every scholar in it, and was granted an expansiveness and height of expression not known from others, such that he made the mention of Sahban forgotten. He excelled his peers in it, bore the Quran, and rendered the eloquent speakers incapable, exceeding description and limit. Everyone who heard of him or saw his trace, when they witnessed him, acknowledged that his reported news far exceeds the report and surpasses what was known of the trace. He would deliver lessons, each of which would fill quires and papers, without stumbling over a word or needing to correct himself ten times repeatedly. He was like the striking lightning with a matching voice like the roaring thunder, in which the outstanding become exhausted and the pretentious deep ones cannot reach his level. What is found in his books of expressions reaching the essence of eloquence is only a drop from the flood of what was on his tongue and a handful from the waves of what was known of his eloquence. He studied fiqh in his youth under his father, Rukn al-Islam, who took pride in his rising, his attainment, the excellence of his intellect, and the cleverness of his nature, due to the signs he saw in him. So he succeeded him after his death and went through all his works, turning them over, and derived some issues from others, and taught for years, and was not satisfied in his youth with taqlid of his father and his companions. He took to verification, striving and exerting in the madhhab, ikhtilaf, and assemblies of debate, until his brilliance became apparent.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account praising Imam al-Juwayni's extraordinary qualities. It begins by introducing his lineage and title 'Imam al-Haramayn' (Imam of the Two Sanctuaries). The author then describes his unmatched eloquence and mastery of Arabic, comparing his speech to lightning and thunder, and noting that his written words are only a fraction of his oral eloquence. The passage then details his early education under his father, Rukn al-Islam, who recognized his talent. After his father's death, he thoroughly studied his works and went beyond mere taqlid, engaging in verification and debate until his brilliance emerged.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Juwayni combined inherited imamate with personal verification, achieving unmatched eloquence and scholarly authority.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that al-Juwayni’s written words are only a drop from the ocean of his eloquence. If your own knowledge could be measured, would your written output reflect a flood or just a trickle? What would it take for you to cultivate such depth that your every word carried weight?
?
Al-Juwayni was not satisfied with merely inheriting his father's scholarship; he engaged in verification and personal struggle. In what area of your deen are you coasting on someone else's efforts (a teacher, a book, a video) without doing the hard work of personal investigation? Will you take one concrete step toward independent learning this week?
?
The scholars of east and west unanimously recognized al-Juwayni’s imamate. But recognition from others is not the goal—it is a byproduct of sincerity and excellence. In your own life, are you seeking the pleasure of Allah by mastering what He has given you, or are you seeking the praise of people? What would change if you focused only on His approval?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

Early Life and Dedication to Knowledge
Al-Juwayni's early striving in teaching and learning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Juwayni's early dedication to study and teaching set the foundation for his later authority.

Core Idea
Al-Juwayni's youth was defined by relentless study and teaching.

After his father's death, the young al-Juwayni did not rest on his lineage. He immediately began teaching, but also pursued studies under multiple shaykhs, combining his own lesson with attending others. This lesson traces his early routine and his extraordinary effort in acquiring knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the sequence of actions: teaching, studying, attending shaykhs, and his personal study.
2
Identify his daily routine
Pay attention to how he structured his day: teaching his own lesson, then going to school of al-Bayhaqi, studying under al-Isfarayini, and attending the mosque of al-Khabbazi for Quran recitation.
He also spent his inheritance on stipends for students.
3
Reflect on his dedication
Consider the phrase 'he would join night with day in study' and his claim of studying a hundred volumes alone. This shows his extraordinary effort.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولاح على أيامه همة أبيه وفراسته ، وسلك طريق المباحثة وجمع الطرق بالمطالعة والمناظرة والمناقشة حتى أربى على المتقدمين وأنسى تصرفات الأولين وسعى في دين الله سعياً يبقى أثره إلى يوم الدين

ابتداء أمره أنه لما توفى أبوه كان سنه دون العشرين أو قريباً منه فأقعد مكانه للتدريس فكان يقيم الرسم في درسه ويقوم منه ويخرج إلى مدرسة البيهقى حتى حصل الأصول وأصول الفقه على الأستاذ الإمام أبي القسم الأسكاف الاسفرايني ، وكان يواظب على مجلسه وقد سمعته يقول في أثناء كلامه : كنت علقت عليه في الأصول أجزاء معدودة وطالعت في نفسى مائة مجلدة ، وكان يصل الليل بالنهار في التحصيل حتى فرغ منه ويبكر كل يوم قبل الاشتغال بدرس نفسه إلى مسجد الأستاذ أبي عبد الله الخبازى يقرأ عليه القرآن ويقتبس من كل نوع من العلوم ما يمكنه مع مواظبته على التدريس وينفق ما ورثه وما كان له من الدخل على أجراء المتفقهة ويجتهد في ذلك ويواظب على المناظرة ، إلى أن ظهر التعصب بين الفريقين واضطربت الأحوال والأمور فاضطر إلى السفر والخروج عن البلد ، فخرج مع المشايخ إلى المعسكر وخرج إلى بغداد يطوف مع المعسكر ويلتقي بالاكابر من العلماء ، ويدارسهم ويناظرهم حتى تهذب في النظر وشاع ذكره ثم خرج إلى الحجاز وجاور بمكة أربع سنين يدرس ويفتي ويجمع طرق المذهب ، ويقبل على التحصيل إلى أن أتفق رجوعه بعد مضى نوبة التعصب فعاد إلى نيسابور وقد ظهر نوبة ولاية السلطان البارسلان وتزين وجه الملك باشارة نظام الملك ، واستقرت أمور الفريقين وانقطع التعصب فعاد إلى التدريس وكان بالغاً في العلم نهايته مستجمعا أسبابه ، فبنيت المدرسة الميمونة النظامية ، وأقعد للتدريس فيها واستقامت أمور الطلبة وبقى على ذلك قريباً من ثلاثين سنة غير مزاحم ولا مدافع ، مسلم له المحراب والمنبر والخطابة والتدريس ومجلس التذكير يوم الجمعة والمناظرة وهجرت له المجالس وانغمر غيره من الفقهاء بعلمه وتسلطه، وكسرت الأسواق في جنبه ونفق سوق المحققين من خواصه وتلامذته وظهرت تصانيفه ، وحضر درسه الأكابر والجمع العظيم من الطلبة وكان يقعد بين يديه كل يوم نحو من ثلاثمائة رجل من الأئمة
And the ambition and perspicacity of his father shone upon his days. He followed the path of investigation and collected the methods through reading, debate and discussion until he surpassed the predecessors and made forgotten the methods of the earlier ones, and strove in the religion of Allah with an endeavor whose trace remains until the Day of Judgment. The beginning of his affair: when his father died, he was less than twenty years old or close to it. So he sat in his place for teaching. He would perform the formalities in his lesson, then leave and go to the school of al-Bayhaqi until he mastered the principles and principles of fiqh under the teacher imam Abu al-Qasim al-Isfak al-Isfarayini. He would attend his sessions regularly, and I heard him say during his speech: 'I studied under him in the principles a few parts, and I studied by myself a hundred volumes.' He would join night with day in study until he finished, and would go early every day before occupying himself with his own lesson to the mosque of the teacher Abu 'Abd Allah al-Khabbazi to recite the Quran to him, and he would acquire from every type of knowledge what he could, while also being regular in teaching. He spent the inheritance he had and the income he had on the stipends of the fuqaha', and he exerted effort in that and was regular in debate. Until partisanship appeared between the two groups and conditions and affairs became disordered, so he was forced to travel and leave the city. He left with the shaykhs to the military camp and left for Baghdad, traveling with the camp and meeting the great scholars, studying with them and debating them until he became refined in debate and his fame spread. Then he left for the Hijaz and stayed in Makka for four years, teaching, giving fatwa, and collecting the methods of the madhhab, and devoting himself to study. Until it happened that he returned after the period of partisanship had passed. He returned to Naysabur, when the period of the reign of Sultan Alp Arslan had appeared and the face of the kingdom was adorned by the indication of Nizam al-Mulk. The affairs of the two groups settled and partisanship ceased. So he returned to teaching, and he had reached the utmost in knowledge and gathered its causes. The blessed Nizamiyya school was built, and he sat for teaching in it. The affairs of the students became stable, and he remained on that for nearly thirty years, without opposition or obstruction. The mihrab, minbar, khutba, teaching, and the assembly of reminder on Friday and debate were conceded to him. Gatherings were abandoned for him, and other fuqaha' were submerged by his knowledge and his dominance. The markets were broken in his presence, and the market of the investigators among his special students and disciples thrived. His works appeared. The great ones and a huge gathering of students attended his lesson, and about three hundred men of the imams would sit before him every day.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage narrates the career of Imam al-Juwayni. It opens by noting his father's ambition and perspicacity. The narrative then details his early teaching after his father's death, his rigorous schedule combining his own lesson, studying under various shaykhs (including Abu al-Qasim al-Isfak al-Isfarayini and Abu 'Abd Allah al-Khabbazi), and his dedication to debate. Political partisanship forced him to travel to Baghdad and then to the Hijaz, where he stayed in Makka for four years. After partisanship ended, he returned to Naysabur under the reign of Sultan Alp Arslan and with the support of Nizam al-Mulk. He was appointed to the Nizamiyya school and taught there for nearly thirty years, enjoying undisputed authority. The passage concludes with his dominance, the large number of students, and the productivity of his scholarly output.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Juwayni inherited his scholarly position without effort.
Correction: The text shows he worked extremely hard, studying under multiple teachers, spending his wealth on students, and combining teaching with personal study.
