Key Takeaway
Al-Juwayni's early career combined teaching, intensive study, and financial generosity, setting the stage for his later eminence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are not yet twenty years old. What have you actually sacrificed for knowledge? Al-Juwayni, at that age, took over his father's teaching post, studied under multiple scholars, read a hundred volumes on his own, and spent his inheritance on others. Where is your equivalent effort?
?
Al-Juwayni joined night with day in study. When was the last time you stayed up late for the sake of learning your religion, not for entertainment or worldly gain? What does that say about your priorities?
?
He spent his inheritance on the stipends of the fuqaha'. What is the most valuable thing you possess, and are you willing to spend it for the sake of knowledge and supporting others in seeking it? If not, why?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
4 min
Travels Due to Partisanship
Al-Juwayni's forced travel and scholarly activities during exile.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how political partisanship forced al-Juwayni to leave Naysabur and how his travels to Baghdad and Mecca enriched his scholarship.

Core Idea
Partisanship scattered the scholars, but al-Juwayni turned exile into opportunity.

The outbreak of partisanship between different groups disrupted the scholarly community in Naysabur. Al-Juwayni was compelled to leave, first with the military camp to Baghdad, then to the Hijaz. He spent four years in Mecca, teaching and studying. This lesson covers that transformative period.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the exile
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the cause (partisanship) and his departure.
2
Trace his travels
He left for Baghdad with the camp, then traveled to the Hijaz and stayed in Mecca for four years.
3
Consider the benefits of travel
Despite the disruption, he met great scholars, studied, debated, and refined his thought.
His fame spread during this period.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولاح على أيامه همة أبيه وفراسته ، وسلك طريق المباحثة وجمع الطرق بالمطالعة والمناظرة والمناقشة حتى أربى على المتقدمين وأنسى تصرفات الأولين وسعى في دين الله سعياً يبقى أثره إلى يوم الدين

ابتداء أمره أنه لما توفى أبوه كان سنه دون العشرين أو قريباً منه فأقعد مكانه للتدريس فكان يقيم الرسم في درسه ويقوم منه ويخرج إلى مدرسة البيهقى حتى حصل الأصول وأصول الفقه على الأستاذ الإمام أبي القسم الأسكاف الاسفرايني ، وكان يواظب على مجلسه وقد سمعته يقول في أثناء كلامه : كنت علقت عليه في الأصول أجزاء معدودة وطالعت في نفسى مائة مجلدة ، وكان يصل الليل بالنهار في التحصيل حتى فرغ منه ويبكر كل يوم قبل الاشتغال بدرس نفسه إلى مسجد الأستاذ أبي عبد الله الخبازى يقرأ عليه القرآن ويقتبس من كل نوع من العلوم ما يمكنه مع مواظبته على التدريس وينفق ما ورثه وما كان له من الدخل على أجراء المتفقهة ويجتهد في ذلك ويواظب على المناظرة ، إلى أن ظهر التعصب بين الفريقين واضطربت الأحوال والأمور فاضطر إلى السفر والخروج عن البلد ، فخرج مع المشايخ إلى المعسكر وخرج إلى بغداد يطوف مع المعسكر ويلتقي بالاكابر من العلماء ، ويدارسهم ويناظرهم حتى تهذب في النظر وشاع ذكره ثم خرج إلى الحجاز وجاور بمكة أربع سنين يدرس ويفتي ويجمع طرق المذهب ، ويقبل على التحصيل إلى أن أتفق رجوعه بعد مضى نوبة التعصب فعاد إلى نيسابور وقد ظهر نوبة ولاية السلطان البارسلان وتزين وجه الملك باشارة نظام الملك ، واستقرت أمور الفريقين وانقطع التعصب فعاد إلى التدريس وكان بالغاً في العلم نهايته مستجمعا أسبابه ، فبنيت المدرسة الميمونة النظامية ، وأقعد للتدريس فيها واستقامت أمور الطلبة وبقى على ذلك قريباً من ثلاثين سنة غير مزاحم ولا مدافع ، مسلم له المحراب والمنبر والخطابة والتدريس ومجلس التذكير يوم الجمعة والمناظرة وهجرت له المجالس وانغمر غيره من الفقهاء بعلمه وتسلطه، وكسرت الأسواق في جنبه ونفق سوق المحققين من خواصه وتلامذته وظهرت تصانيفه ، وحضر درسه الأكابر والجمع العظيم من الطلبة وكان يقعد بين يديه كل يوم نحو من ثلاثمائة رجل من الأئمة
And the ambition and perspicacity of his father shone upon his days. He followed the path of investigation and collected the methods through reading, debate and discussion until he surpassed the predecessors and made forgotten the methods of the earlier ones, and strove in the religion of Allah with an endeavor whose trace remains until the Day of Judgment. The beginning of his affair: when his father died, he was less than twenty years old or close to it. So he sat in his place for teaching. He would perform the formalities in his lesson, then leave and go to the school of al-Bayhaqi until he mastered the principles and principles of fiqh under the teacher imam Abu al-Qasim al-Isfak al-Isfarayini. He would attend his sessions regularly, and I heard him say during his speech: 'I studied under him in the principles a few parts, and I studied by myself a hundred volumes.' He would join night with day in study until he finished, and would go early every day before occupying himself with his own lesson to the mosque of the teacher Abu 'Abd Allah al-Khabbazi to recite the Quran to him, and he would acquire from every type of knowledge what he could, while also being regular in teaching. He spent the inheritance he had and the income he had on the stipends of the fuqaha', and he exerted effort in that and was regular in debate. Until partisanship appeared between the two groups and conditions and affairs became disordered, so he was forced to travel and leave the city. He left with the shaykhs to the military camp and left for Baghdad, traveling with the camp and meeting the great scholars, studying with them and debating them until he became refined in debate and his fame spread. Then he left for the Hijaz and stayed in Makka for four years, teaching, giving fatwa, and collecting the methods of the madhhab, and devoting himself to study. Until it happened that he returned after the period of partisanship had passed. He returned to Naysabur, when the period of the reign of Sultan Alp Arslan had appeared and the face of the kingdom was adorned by the indication of Nizam al-Mulk. The affairs of the two groups settled and partisanship ceased. So he returned to teaching, and he had reached the utmost in knowledge and gathered its causes. The blessed Nizamiyya school was built, and he sat for teaching in it. The affairs of the students became stable, and he remained on that for nearly thirty years, without opposition or obstruction. The mihrab, minbar, khutba, teaching, and the assembly of reminder on Friday and debate were conceded to him. Gatherings were abandoned for him, and other fuqaha' were submerged by his knowledge and his dominance. The markets were broken in his presence, and the market of the investigators among his special students and disciples thrived. His works appeared. The great ones and a huge gathering of students attended his lesson, and about three hundred men of the imams would sit before him every day.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage narrates the career of Imam al-Juwayni. It opens by noting his father's ambition and perspicacity. The narrative then details his early teaching after his father's death, his rigorous schedule combining his own lesson, studying under various shaykhs (including Abu al-Qasim al-Isfak al-Isfarayini and Abu 'Abd Allah al-Khabbazi), and his dedication to debate. Political partisanship forced him to travel to Baghdad and then to the Hijaz, where he stayed in Makka for four years. After partisanship ended, he returned to Naysabur under the reign of Sultan Alp Arslan and with the support of Nizam al-Mulk. He was appointed to the Nizamiyya school and taught there for nearly thirty years, enjoying undisputed authority. The passage concludes with his dominance, the large number of students, and the productivity of his scholarly output.

Key Terms
التعصب
المناظرة
بغداد
الحجاز
مكة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Juwayni's travels were purely a hardship that hindered his scholarship.
Correction: The travels allowed him to meet scholars, refine his skills, and spread his fame, ultimately benefiting his career.

Checkpoint
How many years did al-Juwayni stay in Mecca?
A) 2 years
B) 3 years
C) 4 years
D) 5 years

Key Takeaway
Al-Juwayni's forced exile became a period of intense scholarly activity that enhanced his reputation and knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When conflict or disorder arises in your environment, what is your first impulse? Do you see it as an obstacle or as an opportunity to grow? Al-Juwayni turned forced exile into a period of intense study. What 'exile' in your own life—whether physical, emotional, or spiritual—can you transform into a time of deepening your knowledge and practice?
?
Al-Juwayni traveled with shaykhs and met scholars, not isolating himself. In your pursuit of learning, do you actively seek companions and teachers, or do you try to go it alone? Who are the 'shaykhs' you can travel with or learn from today?
?
Al-Juwayni devoted himself to study in Mecca for four years. If you had four years of uninterrupted time, what would you devote yourself to learning? What would need to change in your life to make that a reality, even on a smaller scale?

Triumphant Return and the Nizamiyya Years
Al-Juwayni's return and establishment at the Nizamiyya school.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Juwayni returned under the patronage of Nizam al-Mulk and reached the peak of his career at the Nizamiyya school.

Core Idea
With patronage and peace, al-Juwayni's knowledge found its full expression.

After the period of partisanship ended, al-Juwayni returned to Naysabur during the reign of Alp Arslan and with the support of Nizam al-Mulk. The Nizamiyya school was built for him, and he taught there for nearly thirty years. This lesson describes his undisputed authority and the flourishing of his teaching and writings.

Guided Path
1
Read the return passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the political background: Alp Arslan and Nizam al-Mulk.
2
Identify his role at Nizamiyya
The Nizamiyya was built for him. He taught there for nearly thirty years without opposition.
3
Note his authority
He was given the mihrab, minbar, khutba, teaching, and the Friday reminder. Other fuqaha' were submerged by his dominance.
4
Reflect on the scale
About 300 imams sat before him daily. His works appeared, and the market of investigators thrived.

?

?

?

Are you maximizing them or neglecting them due to laziness, distraction, or ingratitude? Commit to one action this week to make full use of one such opportunity.

From Father's Legacy to Scholarly Mastery
Narrative of the scholar's early life and education.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the scholar's early life after his father's death laid the foundation for his extraordinary scholarly achievements.

Core Idea
Grief turned to purpose: a young teacher's relentless pursuit of knowledge.

This passage opens the biography by showing how the scholar inherited his father's ambition and quickly established himself as a teacher despite his youth. We see his rigorous study routine, his mastery of usul and usul al-fiqh under a prominent teacher, and the remarkable dedication that would define his entire career.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the sequence of events: the father's death, taking up teaching, studying with Abu al-Qasim, and the intense study schedule.
The phrase 'he would connect night to day in study' is a key indication of his dedication.
2
Identify the stages of early education
Identify three stages: 1) sitting in his father's place for teaching, 2) studying usul with Abu al-Qasim, 3) his personal study of one hundred volumes and Quran recitation with al-Khabbazi.
3
Reflect on the meaning of 'mastery'
Ask yourself what it meant to 'master usul' in that era. This involved not only learning but also debating and investigating methods.
This ties into the learning objective.

الطلبة وتخرج به جماعة من الأئمة والفحول وأولاد الصدور ، حتى بلغوا محل التدريس في زمانه وانتظم بإقباله على العلم ومواظبته على التدريس والمناظرة والمباحثة أسباب ومحافل ومجامع وإمعان في طلب العلم وسوق نافقة لأهله لم يعهد قبله واتصل به ما يليق بمنصبه من القبول عند السلطان والوزير والأركان ووفور الحشمة عندهم بحيث لا يذكر غيره فكان المخاطب والمشار إليه والمقبول من قبله والمهجور من هجره والمصدر في المجالس من ينتمي إلى خدمته والمنظور إليه من يغترف في الأصول والفروع من طريقته ، واتفق منه تصانيف برسم الحضرة النظامية مثل النظامي والغياثي وإنفاذها إلى الحضرة ووقوعها موقع القبول ومقابلتها بما يليق بها من الشكر والرضى ، والخلع الفائقة والمراكب المثمنة والهدايا والمرسومات وكذلك إلى أن قلد زعامة الأصحاب ورياسة الطائفة وفوض إليه أمور الأوقاف وصارت حشمته وزر العلماء والأئمة والقضاة وقوله في الفتوى مرجع العظماء والأكابر والولاة ، واتفقت له نهضة في أعلى ما كان من أيامه إلى أصبهان لسبب مخالفة بعض الأصحاب فلقى بها من المجلس النظامي ما كان من اللائق بمنصبه من الاستبشار والاعزاز والاكرام بأنواع المبار وأجيب بما كان فوق مطلوبه وعاد مكرماً إلى نيسابور ، وصار أكثر عنايته مصروفاً إلى تصنيف المذهب الكبير المسمى ( نهاية المطلب في دراية المذهب ) حتى حرره وأملاه وأتى فيه من البحث والتقدير والسبك والتنقير والتدقيق والتحقيق بما شفى الغليل وأوضح السبيل ونبه على قدره ومحله في علم الشريعة ، ودرس للخواص من التلامذه وفرغ منه ومن إتمامه فعقد مجلساً لتتمة الكتاب حضره الأئمة والكبار وختم الكتاب على رسم الإملاء والاستملاء، وتبجح الجماعة بذلك ودعوا له واثنوا عليه وكان من المعتدين بإتمام ذلك الشاكرين الله عليه فما صنف في الإسلام قبله مثله ولا أتفق لأحد ما أتفق له ، ومن قاس طريقته بطريقة المتقدمين في الأصول والفروع وأنصف أقر بعلو منصبه ووفور تعبه ونصبه في الدين وكثرة سهره في استنباط الغوامض وتحقيق المسائل وترتيب الدلائل
His father's ambition and sagacity appeared in his days, and he followed the path of investigation and collected methods through reading, debate, and discussion until he surpassed the predecessors and made the actions of the earlier ones forgotten, and he strove in the religion of God with a striving whose effect remains until the Day of Judgment. The beginning of his affair was that when his father died, his age was under twenty or close to it, so he sat in his place for teaching. He would maintain the formal procedure in his lesson and then leave it and go to the school of al-Bayhaqi until he mastered usul (principles) and usul al-fiqh (principles of jurisprudence) under the teacher, the Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Askaf al-Isfara'ini. He attended his sessions regularly, and I heard him say during his speech: 'I completed with him in usul a few volumes, and I read with myself one hundred volumes.' He would connect night to day in study until he finished, and he would go early every day before occupying himself with his own lesson to the mosque of the teacher Abu 'Abd Allah al-Khabbazi, reciting the Qur'an to him and acquiring from every type of knowledge what he could, while regularly attending to teaching. He spent what he inherited and what income he had on paying the faqih students, and he strove in that and persisted in debate, until partisanship appeared between the two groups and conditions and affairs became disturbed, so he was forced to travel and leave the city. He left with the shaykhs to the military camp and went to Baghdad, touring with the camp and meeting the senior scholars, studying and debating with them until his insight was refined and his reputation spread. Then he left for the Hijaz and stayed in Mecca for four years, teaching, giving fatwas, and collecting the methods of the school, and he focused on study until his return happened after the period of partisanship passed. He returned to Nishapur, and the period of the rule of Sultan Alp Arslan had appeared, and the face of the kingdom was adorned by the suggestion of Nizam al-Mulk. The affairs of the two groups stabilized, partisanship ended, and he returned to teaching. He had reached the ultimate in knowledge, gathering its causes. The blessed Nizamiyya school was built, and he sat for teaching in it, and the affairs of the students were put in order. He remained in that state for nearly thirty years, undisturbed and unchallenged. The sanctuary pulpit, sermon, teaching, the Friday reminder session, and debate were all conceded to him. Other jurists were submerged by his knowledge and authority. Markets were broken beside him, and the market of the researchers among his special students and disciples became brisk. His works appeared. The senior scholars and a great multitude of students attended his lesson, and about three hundred men of the imams and students would sit before him every day. A group of imams, outstanding scholars, and sons of the dignitaries graduated under him until they reached the place of teaching in his time. With his attention to knowledge and his persistence in teaching, debate, and investigation, he organized gatherings, assemblies, and deep engagement in seeking knowledge, and a thriving market for its people that had not been known before him. There came to him what was worthy of his position of acceptance from the sultan, the vizier, and the pillars of state, and abundant dignity before them, such that no other was mentioned. He was the addressee, the one pointed to, the one accepted, the one whose abandonment was abandonment. The one who belonged to his service was the authority in assemblies, and the one who drew from his way in usul and furu' was looked to. He produced works by order of the Nizamiyya court, such as al-Nizami and al-Ghiyathi, and sent them to the court, where they met with acceptance and were met with appropriate gratitude and satisfaction, along with excellent robes of honor, expensive mounts, gifts, and stipends. Likewise, he was entrusted with the leadership of the companions and the headship of the sect, and the affairs of endowments were delegated to him. His dignity weighed heavily upon the scholars, imams, and judges, and his word in fatwa was the reference for the great ones, the senior scholars, and the governors. He made a journey in the highest of his days to Isfahan due to the opposition of some companions. There he met with the Nizamiyya council what was fitting for his position: glad tidings, honor, and generosity of various kinds of kindness, and he was given above what he desired. He returned honored to Nishapur. His greater attention became directed to composing the great work of the school called Nihayat al-Matlab fi Dirayat al-Madhhab until he edited it and dictated it, bringing to it of research, estimation, refined wording, critical examination, verification, and investigation what quenched the thirst, clarified the path, and drew attention to its worth and station in the science of Shari'a. He taught it to the special students and finished it. Upon its completion, he held a session for the completion of the book, attended by imams and senior figures, and he concluded the book in the manner of dictation and transcription. The group rejoiced at that, prayed for him, and praised him. He was among those who acknowledged the completion, thanking God for it. No book like it has been composed in Islam before him, nor did what happened for him happen for anyone else. Whoever compares his way to the way of the predecessors in usul and furu' and is fair will acknowledge the height of his station, the abundance of his effort and exertion in religion, and his frequent staying awake in extracting subtle points, verifying issues, and arranging proofs.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of a scholar's life, detailing his early education, teaching career, travels, scholarly output, and recognition. Ibn 'Asakir narrates how the scholar, after his father's death, took up teaching while still young, studying with prominent teachers and dedicating himself day and night to learning. He faced sectarian conflict, which forced him to travel to Baghdad and Mecca, where he continued to study and teach. After the conflict subsided, he returned to Nishapur and was appointed to teach at the newly built Nizamiyya school, where he remained for nearly thirty years, attracting large numbers of students and producing influential works. The passage emphasizes his authority in teaching, his acceptance by rulers, and his monumental work 'Nihayat al-Matlab,' which was unparalleled. It concludes by asserting that anyone who fairly compares his method to earlier scholars will recognize his high rank and immense effort.

Key Terms
أصول
أصول الفقه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How old was the scholar when his father died?
A) Over thirty
B) Under twenty or close to it
C) Exactly twenty-five
D) His exact age is not mentioned

Key Takeaway
The scholar's early dedication to learning and teaching, even after his father's death, set the stage for his future greatness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This scholar, at under twenty, was already teaching and studying day and night. You have the same age—what are you currently teaching or learning for the sake of your religion? If nothing, what is holding you back from starting today?
?
The scholar would go to a teacher before his own lesson every morning. What is the first thing you do each day? Is it for your own growth or just routine? Will you commit to beginning your day with an act of learning or worship from tomorrow?
?
He read one hundred volumes on his own while studying just a few with his teacher. How much do you read and reflect on religious texts outside of formal settings? Are you content with minimal effort? What one change can you make to replace idle time with beneficial reading?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
5 min
Overcoming Trials: Travel and Return to Nishapur
Narrative of the scholar's travels during sectarian conflict and his return to Nishapur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the scholar navigated sectarian conflict and used travel to refine his knowledge and reputation.

Core Idea
Adversity became a stepping stone: travel, study, and return to a stable teaching post.

This lesson covers the scholar's journey through difficult times. After mastering the basics, he faced partisanship that forced him to travel. He visited Baghdad, met senior scholars, spent four years in Mecca teaching and studying, and eventually returned to Nishapur when the political climate changed. His return coincided with the rise of Nizam al-Mulk, leading to his appointment at the newly built Nizamiyya school.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about travel and return
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the turning point: from partisanship forcing travel to the return when the sultan's rule stabilized.
The phrase 'partisanship appeared between the two groups' refers to sectarian conflict.
2
Trace the geographic journey
Identify the places he went: Nishapur, Baghdad, Mecca, and back to Nishapur. Consider how each location contributed to his growth.
Mecca was a place of intense study and teaching for four years.
3
Understand the political context
Note the mention of Sultan Alp Arslan and Nizam al-Mulk. The scholar's return was enabled by the end of partisanship and the new vizier's support.
This shows how the scholar's life intertwined with political events.

Source Text

ولاح على أيامه همة أبيه وفراسته ، وسلك طريق المباحثة وجمع الطرق بالمطالعة والمناظرة والمناقشة حتى أربى على المتقدمين وأنسى تصرفات الأولين وسعى في دين الله سعياً يبقى أثره إلى يوم الدين. ابتداء أمره أنه لما توفى أبوه كان سنه دون العشرين أو قريباً منه فأقعد مكانه للتدريس فكان يقيم الرسم في درسه ويقوم منه ويخرج إلى مدرسة البيهقى حتى حصل الأصول وأصول الفقه على الأستاذ الإمام أبي القسم الأسكاف الاسفرايني ، وكان يواظب على مجلسه وقد سمعته يقول في أثناء كلامه : كنت علقت عليه في الأصول أجزاء معدودة وطالعت في نفسى مائة مجلدة ، وكان يصل الليل بالنهار في التحصيل حتى فرغ منه ويبكر كل يوم قبل الاشتغال بدرس نفسه إلى مسجد الأستاذ أبي عبد الله الخبازى يقرأ عليه القرآن ويقتبس من كل نوع من العلوم ما يمكنه مع مواظبته على التدريس وينفق ما ورثه وما كان له من الدخل على إجراء المتفقهة ويجتهد في ذلك ويواظب على المناظرة ، إلى أن ظهر التعصب بين الفريقين واضطربت الأحوال والأمور فاضطر إلى السفر والخروج عن البلد ، فخرج مع المشايخ إلى المعسكر وخرج إلى بغداد يطوف مع المعسكر ويلتقي بالاكابر من العلماء ، ويدارسهم ويناظرهم حتى تهذب في النظر وشاع ذكره ثم خرج إلى الحجاز وجاور بمكة أربع سنين يدرس ويفتى ويجمع طرق المذهب ، ويقبل على التحصيل إلى أن أتفق رجوعه بعد مضى نوبة التعصب فعاد إلى نيسابور وقد ظهر نوبة ولاية السلطان البارسلان وتزين وجه الملك بإشارة نظام الملك ، واستقرت أمور الفريقين وانقطع التعصب فعاد إلى التدريس وكان بالغاً في العلم نهايته مستجمعا أسبابه ، فبنيت المدرسة الميمونة النظامية ، وأقعد للتدريس فيها واستقامت أمور الطلبة وبقى على ذلك قريباً من ثلاثين سنة غير مزاحم ولا مدافع ، مسلم له المحراب والمنبر والخطابة والتدريس ومجلس التذكير يوم الجمعة والمناظرة وهجرت له المجالس وانغمر غيره من الفقهاء بعلمه وتسلطه، وكسرت الأسواق في جنبه ونفق سوق المحققين من خواصه وتلامذته وظهرت تصانيفه ، وحضر درسه الأكابر والجمع العظيم من الطلبة وكان يقعد بين يديه كل يوم نحو من ثلاثماية رجل من الأئمة ومن الطلبة وتخرج به جماعة من الأئمة والفحول وأولاد الصدور ، حتى بلغوا محل التدريس في زمانه وانتظم بإقباله على العلم ومواظبته على التدريس والمناظرة والمباحثة أسباب ومحافل ومجامع وإمعان في طلب العلم وسوق نافقة لأهله لم يعهد قبله واتصل به ما يليق بمنصبه من القبول عند السلطان والوزير والأركان ووفور الحشمة عندهم بحيث لا يذكر غيره فكان المخاطب والمشار إليه والمقبول من قبله والمهجور من هجره والمصدر في المجالس من ينتمي إلى خدمته والمنظور إليه من يغترف في الأصول والفروع من طريقته ، واتفق منه تصانيف برسم الحضرة النظامية مثل النظامي والغياثي وإنفاذها إلى الحضرة ووقوعها موقع القبول ومقابلتها بما يليق بها من الشكر والرضى ، والخلع الفائقة والمراكب المثمنة والهدايا والمرسومات وكذلك إلى أن قلد زعامة الأصحاب ورياسة الطائفة وفوض إليه أمور الأوقاف وصارت حشمته وزر العلماء والأئمة والقضاة وقوله في الفتوى مرجع العظماء والأكابر والولاة ، واتفقت له نهضة في أعلى ما كان من أيامه إلى أصبهان لسبب مخالفة بعض الأصحاب فلقى بها من المجلس النظامي ما كان من اللائق بمنصبه من الاستبشار والاعزاز والاكرام بأنواع المبار وأجيب بما كان فوق مطلوبه وعاد مكرماً إلى نيسابور ، وصار أكثر عنايته مصروفاً إلى تصنيف المذهب الكبير المسمى ( نهاية المطلب في دراية المذهب ) حتى حرره وأملاه وأتى فيه من البحث والتقدير والسبك والتنقير والتدقيق والتحقيق بما شفى الغليل وأوضح السبيل ونبه على قدره ومحله في علم الشريعة ، ودرس للخواص من التلامذه وفرغ منه ومن إتمامه فعقد مجلساً لتتمة الكتاب حضره الأئمة والكبار وختم الكتاب على رسم الإملاء والاستملاء، وتبجح الجماعة بذلك ودعوا له واثنوا عليه وكان من المعتدين بإتمام ذلك الشاكرين الله عليه فما صنف في الإسلام قبله مثله ولا أتفق لأحد ما أتفق له ، ومن قاس طريقته بطريقة المتقدمين في الأصول والفروع وأنصف أقر بعلو منصبه ووفور تعبه ونصبه في الدين وكثرة سهره في استنباط الغوامض وتحقيق المسائل وترتيب الدلائل
His father's ambition and sagacity appeared in his days, and he followed the path of investigation and collected methods through reading, debate, and discussion until he surpassed the predecessors and made the actions of the earlier ones forgotten, and he strove in the religion of God with a striving whose effect remains until the Day of Judgment. The beginning of his affair was that when his father died, his age was under twenty or close to it, so he sat in his place for teaching. He would maintain the formal procedure in his lesson and then leave it and go to the school of al-Bayhaqi until he mastered usul (principles) and usul al-fiqh (principles of jurisprudence) under the teacher, the Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Askaf al-Isfara'ini. He attended his sessions regularly, and I heard him say during his speech: 'I completed with him in usul a few volumes, and I read with myself one hundred volumes.' He would connect night to day in study until he finished, and he would go early every day before occupying himself with his own lesson to the mosque of the teacher Abu 'Abd Allah al-Khabbazi, reciting the Qur'an to him and acquiring from every type of knowledge what he could, while regularly attending to teaching. He spent what he inherited and what income he had on paying the faqih students, and he strove in that and persisted in debate, until partisanship appeared between the two groups and conditions and affairs became disturbed, so he was forced to travel and leave the city. He left with the shaykhs to the military camp and went to Baghdad, touring with the camp and meeting the senior scholars, studying and debating with them until his insight was refined and his reputation spread. Then he left for the Hijaz and stayed in Mecca for four years, teaching, giving fatwas, and collecting the methods of the school, and he focused on study until his return happened after the period of partisanship passed. He returned to Nishapur, and the period of the rule of Sultan Alp Arslan had appeared, and the face of the kingdom was adorned by the suggestion of Nizam al-Mulk. The affairs of the two groups stabilized, partisanship ended, and he returned to teaching. He had reached the ultimate in knowledge, gathering its causes. The blessed Nizamiyya school was built, and he sat for teaching in it, and the affairs of the students were put in order. He remained in that state for nearly thirty years, undisturbed and unchallenged. The sanctuary pulpit, sermon, teaching, the Friday reminder session, and debate were all conceded to him. Other jurists were submerged by his knowledge and authority. Markets were broken beside him, and the market of the researchers among his special students and disciples became brisk. His works appeared. The senior scholars and a great multitude of students attended his lesson, and about three hundred men of the imams and students would sit before him every day. A group of imams, outstanding scholars, and sons of the dignitaries graduated under him until they reached the place of teaching in his time. With his attention to knowledge and his persistence in teaching, debate, and investigation, he organized gatherings, assemblies, and deep engagement in seeking knowledge, and a thriving market for its people that had not been known before him. There came to him what was worthy of his position of acceptance from the sultan, the vizier, and the pillars of state, and abundant dignity before them, such that no other was mentioned. He was the addressee, the one pointed to, the one accepted, the one whose abandonment was abandonment. The one who belonged to his service was the authority in assemblies, and the one who drew from his way in usul and furu' was looked to. He produced works by order of the Nizamiyya court, such as al-Nizami and al-Ghiyathi, and sent them to the court, where they met with acceptance and were met with appropriate gratitude and satisfaction, along with excellent robes of honor, expensive mounts, gifts, and stipends. Likewise, he was entrusted with the leadership of the companions and the headship of the sect, and the affairs of endowments were delegated to him. His dignity weighed heavily upon the scholars, imams, and judges, and his word in fatwa was the reference for the great ones, the senior scholars, and the governors. He made a journey in the highest of his days to Isfahan due to the opposition of some companions. There he met with the Nizamiyya council what was fitting for his position: glad tidings, honor, and generosity of various kinds of kindness, and he was given above what he desired. He taught it to the special students and finished it. Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of a scholar's life, detailing his early education, teaching career, travels, scholarly output, and recognition. Ibn 'Asakir narrates how the scholar, after his father's death, took up teaching while still young, studying with prominent teachers and dedicating himself day and night to learning. He faced sectarian conflict, which forced him to travel to Baghdad and Mecca, where he continued to study and teach. After the conflict subsided, he returned to Nishapur and was appointed to teach at the newly built Nizamiyya school, where he remained for nearly thirty years, attracting large numbers of students and producing influential works. The passage emphasizes his authority in teaching, his acceptance by rulers, and his monumental work 'Nihayat al-Matlab,' which was unparalleled. It concludes by asserting that anyone who fairly compares his method to earlier scholars will recognize his high rank and immense effort.

نظام الملك
المدرسة النظامية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The scholar's travels were primarily for political gain.
Correction: The passage emphasizes his travels were driven by sectarian conflict and his commitment to knowledge, as he spent four years in Mecca teaching and studying, and in Baghdad debating with scholars.

Checkpoint
How long did the scholar teach at the Nizamiyya school according to this passage?
A) Nearly twenty years
B) Nearly thirty years
C) Nearly forty years
D) A lifetime

Key Takeaway
The scholar's travels and return to a stable teaching post under Nizam al-Mulk allowed him to establish a lasting legacy of teaching and learning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The scholar was forced to leave his home due to partisanship. When have you faced a situation where you had to leave comfort behind? Did you see it as a loss or an opportunity for growth? What would change if you chose to see it as a divine opening to deepen your knowledge?
?
He spent four years in Mecca teaching and collecting methods before returning to a stable post. What are you doing right now with the time and resources you have? If you knew you had four years of uncertainty ahead, how would you invest them for your intellectual and spiritual development?
?
He returned only after the partisanship ended, not forcing his way back. Are you patient in waiting for the right conditions, or do you try to force outcomes? What part of your life today requires patience like his, trusting that the right time will come for you to fulfill your purpose?

The Nizamiyya Era: Teaching and Writing the Masterwork
Final account of scholarly output, recognition, and legacy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholar's greatest scholarly contributions, especially his monumental work Nihayat al-Matlab, and the high regard he enjoyed from rulers and scholars.

Core Idea
A legacy etched in ink: the unmatched Nihayat al-Matlab and a life of recognized authority.

This final part of the biography highlights the scholar's later achievements: his compositions commissioned by the Nizamiyya court, his journey to Isfahan to resolve opposition, and above all his magnum opus, Nihayat al-Matlab fi Dirayat al-Madhhab. The passage concludes with a powerful endorsement of his unmatched status and the unparalleled quality of his work.

Guided Path
1

Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note the specific works mentioned: al-Nizami, al-Ghiyathi, and Nihayat al-Matlab.
These works were written for the Nizamiyya court.

Pay attention to the description: 'he brought to it of research, estimation, refined wording...' and the claim that no book like it had been composed before.

ولاح على أيامه همة أبيه وفراسته ، وسلك طريق المباحثة وجمع الطرق بالمطالعة والمناظرة والمناقشة حتى أربى على المتقدمين وأنسى تصرفات الأولين وسعى في دين الله سعياً يبقى أثره إلى يوم الدين. ابتداء أمره أنه لما توفى أبوه كان سنه دون العشرين أو قريباً منه فأقعد مكانه للتدريس فكان يقيم الرسم في درسه ويقوم منه ويخرج إلى مدرسة البيهقى حتى حصل الأصول وأصول الفقه على الأستاذ الإمام أبي القسم الأسكاف الاسفرايني ، وكان يواظب على مجلسه وقد سمعته يقول في أثناء كلامه : كنت علقت عليه في الأصول أجزاء معدودة وطالعت في نفسى مائة مجلدة ، وكان يصل الليل بالنهار في التحصيل حتى فرغ منه ويبكر كل يوم قبل الاشتغال بدرس نفسه إلى مسجد الأستاذ أبي عبد الله الخبازى يقرأ عليه القرآن ويقتبس من كل نوع من العلوم ما يمكنه مع مواظبته على التدريس وينفق ما ورثه وما كان له من الدخل على إجراء المتفقهة ويجتهد في ذلك ويواظب على المناظرة ، إلى أن ظهر التعصب بين الفريقين واضطربت الأحوال والأمور فاضطر إلى السفر والخروج عن البلد ، فخرج مع المشايخ إلى المعسكر وخرج إلى بغداد يطوف مع المعسكر ويلتقي بالاكابر من العلماء ، ويدارسهم ويناظرهم حتى تهذب في النظر وشاع ذكره ثم خرج إلى الحجاز وجاور بمكة أربع سنين يدرس ويفتى ويجمع طرق المذهب ، ويقبل على التحصيل إلى أن أتفق رجوعه بعد مضى نوبة التعصب فعاد إلى نيسابور وقد ظهر نوبة ولاية السلطان البارسلان وتزين وجه الملك بإشارة نظام الملك ، واستقرت أمور الفريقين وانقطع التعصب فعاد إلى التدريس وكان بالغاً في العلم نهايته مستجمعا أسبابه ، فبنيت المدرسة الميمونة النظامية ، وأقعد للتدريس فيها واستقامت أمور الطلبة وبقى على ذلك قريباً من ثلاثين سنة غير مزاحم ولا مدافع ، مسلم له المحراب والمنبر والخطابة والتدريس ومجلس التذكير يوم الجمعة والمناظرة وهجرت له المجالس وانغمر غيره من الفقهاء بعلمه وتسلطه، وكسرت الأسواق في جنبه ونفق سوق المحققين من خواصه وتلامذته وظهرت تصانيفه ، وحضر درسه الأكابر والجمع العظيم من الطلبة وكان يقعد بين يديه كل يوم نحو من ثلاثماية رجل من الأئمة ومن الطلبة وتخرج به جماعة من الأئمة والفحول وأولاد الصدور ، حتى بلغوا محل التدريس في زمانه وانتظم بإقباله على العلم ومواظبته على التدريس والمناظرة والمباحثة أسباب ومحافل ومجامع وإمعان في طلب العلم وسوق نافقة لأهله لم يعهد قبله واتصل به ما يليق بمنصبه من القبول عند السلطان والوزير والأركان ووفور الحشمة عندهم بحيث لا يذكر غيره فكان المخاطب والمشار إليه والمقبول من قبله والمهجور من هجره والمصدر في المجالس من ينتمي إلى خدمته والمنظور إليه من يغترف في الأصول والفروع من طريقته ، واتفق منه تصانيف برسم الحضرة النظامية مثل النظامي والغياثي وإنفاذها إلى الحضرة ووقوعها موقع القبول ومقابلتها بما يليق بها من الشكر والرضى ، والخلع الفائقة والمراكب المثمنة والهدايا والمرسومات وكذلك إلى أن قلد زعامة الأصحاب ورياسة الطائفة وفوض إليه أمور الأوقاف وصارت حشمته وزر العلماء والأئمة والقضاة وقوله في الفتوى مرجع العظماء والأكابر والولاة ، واتفقت له نهضة في أعلى ما كان من أيامه إلى أصبهان لسبب مخالفة بعض الأصحاب فلقى بها من المجلس النظامي ما كان من اللائق بمنصبه من الاستبشار والاعزاز والاكرام بأنواع المبار وأجيب بما كان فوق مطلوبه وعاد مكرماً إلى نيسابور ، وصار أكثر عنايته مصروفاً إلى تصنيف المذهب الكبير المسمى ( نهاية المطلب في دراية المذهب ) حتى حرره وأملاه وأتى فيه من البحث والتقدير والسبك والتنقير والتدقيق والتحقيق بما شفى الغليل وأوضح السبيل ونبه على قدره ومحله في علم الشريعة ، ودرس للخواص من التلامذه وفرغ منه ومن إتمامه فعقد مجلساً لتتمة الكتاب حضره الأئمة والكبار وختم الكتاب على رسم الإملاء والاستملاء، وتبجح الجماعة بذلك ودعوا له واثنوا عليه وكان من المعتدين بإتمام ذلك الشاكرين الله عليه فما صنف في الإسلام قبله مثله ولا أتفق لأحد ما أتفق له ، ومن قاس طريقته بطريقة المتقدمين في الأصول والفروع وأنصف أقر بعلو منصبه ووفور تعبه ونصبه في الدين وكثرة سهره في استنباط الغوامض وتحقيق المسائل وترتيب الدلائل
His father's ambition and sagacity appeared in his days, and he followed the path of investigation and collected methods through reading, debate, and discussion until he surpassed the predecessors and made the actions of the earlier ones forgotten, and he strove in the religion of God with a striving whose effect remains until the Day of Judgment. The beginning of his affair was that when his father died, his age was under twenty or close to it, so he sat in his place for teaching. He would maintain the formal procedure in his lesson and then leave it and go to the school of al-Bayhaqi until he mastered usul (principles) and usul al-fiqh (principles of jurisprudence) under the teacher, the Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Askaf al-Isfara'ini. He attended his sessions regularly, and I heard him say during his speech: 'I completed with him in usul a few volumes, and I read with myself one hundred volumes.' He would connect night to day in study until he finished, and he would go early every day before occupying himself with his own lesson to the mosque of the teacher Abu 'Abd Allah al-Khabbazi, reciting the Qur'an to him and acquiring from every type of knowledge what he could, while regularly attending to teaching. He spent what he inherited and what income he had on paying the faqih students, and he strove in that and persisted in debate, until partisanship appeared between the two groups and conditions and affairs became disturbed, so he was forced to travel and leave the city. He left with the shaykhs to the military camp and went to Baghdad, touring with the camp and meeting the senior scholars, studying and debating with them until his insight was refined and his reputation spread. Then he left for the Hijaz and stayed in Mecca for four years, teaching, giving fatwas, and collecting the methods of the school, and he focused on study until his return happened after the period of partisanship passed. He returned to Nishapur, and the period of the rule of Sultan Alp Arslan had appeared, and the face of the kingdom was adorned by the suggestion of Nizam al-Mulk. The affairs of the two groups stabilized, partisanship ended, and he returned to teaching. He had reached the ultimate in knowledge, gathering its causes. The blessed Nizamiyya school was built, and he sat for teaching in it, and the affairs of the students were put in order. He remained in that state for nearly thirty years, undisturbed and unchallenged. The sanctuary pulpit, sermon, teaching, the Friday reminder session, and debate were all conceded to him. Other jurists were submerged by his knowledge and authority. Markets were broken beside him, and the market of the researchers among his special students and disciples became brisk. His works appeared. The senior scholars and a great multitude of students attended his lesson, and about three hundred men of the imams and students would sit before him every day. A group of imams, outstanding scholars, and sons of the dignitaries graduated under him until they reached the place of teaching in his time. With his attention to knowledge and his persistence in teaching, debate, and investigation, he organized gatherings, assemblies, and deep engagement in seeking knowledge, and a thriving market for its people that had not been known before him. There came to him what was worthy of his position of acceptance from the sultan, the vizier, and the pillars of state, and abundant dignity before them, such that no other was mentioned. He was the addressee, the one pointed to, the one accepted, the one whose abandonment was abandonment. The one who belonged to his service was the authority in assemblies, and the one who drew from his way in usul and furu' was looked to. He produced works by order of the Nizamiyya court, such as al-Nizami and al-Ghiyathi, and sent them to the court, where they met with acceptance and were met with appropriate gratitude and satisfaction, along with excellent robes of honor, expensive mounts, gifts, and stipends. Likewise, he was entrusted with the leadership of the companions and the headship of the sect, and the affairs of endowments were delegated to him. His dignity weighed heavily upon the scholars, imams, and judges, and his word in fatwa was the reference for the great ones, the senior scholars, and the governors. He made a journey in the highest of his days to Isfahan due to the opposition of some companions. There he met with the Nizamiyya council what was fitting for his position: glad tidings, honor, and generosity of various kinds of kindness, and he was given above what he desired. He returned honored to Nishapur. His greater attention became directed to composing the great work of the school called Nihayat al-Matlab fi Dirayat al-Madhhab until he edited it and dictated it, bringing to it of research, estimation, refined wording, critical examination, verification, and investigation what quenched the thirst, clarified the path, and drew attention to its worth and station in the science of Shari'a. He taught it to the special students and finished it. Upon its completion, he held a session for the completion of the book, attended by imams and senior figures, and he concluded the book in the manner of dictation and transcription. The group rejoiced at that, prayed for him, and praised him. He was among those who acknowledged the completion, thanking God for it. No book like it has been composed in Islam before him, nor did what happened for him happen for anyone else. Whoever compares his way to the way of the predecessors in usul and furu' and is fair will acknowledge the height of his station, the abundance of his effort and exertion in religion, and his frequent staying awake in extracting subtle points, verifying issues, and arranging proofs.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of a scholar's life, detailing his early education, teaching career, travels, scholarly output, and recognition. Ibn 'Asakir narrates how the scholar, after his father's death, took up teaching while still young, studying with prominent teachers and dedicating himself day and night to learning. He faced sectarian conflict, which forced him to travel to Baghdad and Mecca, where he continued to study and teach. After the conflict subsided, he returned to Nishapur and was appointed to teach at the newly built Nizamiyya school, where he remained for nearly thirty years, attracting large numbers of students and producing influential works. The passage emphasizes his authority in teaching, his acceptance by rulers, and his monumental work 'Nihayat al-Matlab,' which was unparalleled. It concludes by asserting that anyone who fairly compares his method to earlier scholars will recognize his high rank and immense effort.

The Scholar's Teaching, Prestige, and Major Work
Ibn Asakir describes the scholar's teaching, students, and composition of Nihayat al-Matlab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and contributions of a great Shafi'i scholar as depicted by Ibn Asakir, focusing on his teaching impact, high status, and the composition of his magnum opus, Nihayat al-Matlab.

Core Idea
A scholar's dedication to teaching and his magnum opus set a new standard in Islamic scholarship.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's work introduces us to a towering figure in Islamic scholarship. It details how his teaching produced a generation of scholars, his high status with rulers, and the composition of his masterpiece, Nihayat al-Matlab. We see a model of scholarly excellence that combined teaching, authorship, and influence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the complete Arabic passage and its literal translation to get an overall sense of the scholar's profile. Note the sequence: teaching, status, works, journey, major book.
2
Identify the scholar's teaching impact
Notice how the passage highlights that many students became teachers themselves. This shows the scholar's effectiveness in producing future scholars.
The phrase 'تخرج به جماعة من الأئمة' indicates direct student output.
3
Analyze his relationship with authorities
Observe the details about acceptance by the sultan and viziers. The scholar's word in fatwa was final, and he was given leadership over the group and endowments.
This reflects the integration of scholarship and political power.
4
Understand his major work
Focus on the description of 'Nihayat al-Matlab'. Note the process of composition, the completion session, and the praise it received. The passage claims no such work existed before.
5
Reflect on the overall significance
Consider the final sentence: anyone who compares his method to earlier scholars will acknowledge his lofty station. This sums up the passage's claim of his unparalleled contribution.

الطلبة وتخرج به جماعة من الأئمة والفحول وأولاد الصدور، حتى بلغوا محل التدريس في زمانه وانتظم بإقباله على العلم ومواظبته على التدريس والمناظرة والمباحثة أسباب ومحافل ومجامع وإمعان في طلب العلم وسوق نافقة لأهله لم يعهد قبله وأتصل به ما يليق بمنصبه من القبول عند السلطان والوزير والأركان ووفور الحشمة عندهم بحيث لا يذكر غيره فكان المخاطب والمشار إليه والمقبول من قبله والمهجور من هجره والمصدر في المجالس من ينتمى إلى خدمته والمنظور إليه من يغترف في الأصول والفروع من طريقته، واتفق منه تصانيف برسم الحضرة النظامية مثل النظامي والغياثي وانفاذها إلى الحضرة ووقوعها موقع القبول ومقابلتها بما يليق بها من الشكر والرضى، والخلع الفائقة والمراكب المثمنة والهدايا والمرسومات وكذلك إلى أن قلد زعامة الأصحاب ورياسة الطائفة وفوض إليه أمور الأوقاف وصارت حشمته وزر العلماء والأئمة والقضاة وقوله في الفتوى مرجع العظماء والأكابر والولاة، واتفقت له نهضة في أعلى ما كان من أيامه إلى أصبهان لسبب مخالفة بعض الأصحاب فلقى بها من المجلس النظامي ما كان من اللائق بمنصبه من الاستبشار والاعزاز والاكرام بأنواع المبر وأجيب بما كان فوق مطلوبه وعاد مكرماً إلى نيسابور، وصار أكثر عنايته مصروفاً إلى تصنيف المذهب الكبير المسمى ( نهاية المطلب في دراية المذهب ) حتى حرره وأملاه وأتى فيه من البحث والتقدير والسبك والتنقير والتدقيق والتحقيق بما شفى الغليل وأوضح السبيل ونبه على قدره ومحله في علم الشريعة، ودرس للخواص من التلامذه وفرغ منه ومن إتمامه فعقد مجلساً لتتمة الكتاب حضره الأئمة والكبار وختم الكتاب على رسم الإملاء والاستملاء، وتبجح الجماعة بذلك ودعوا له واثنوا عليه وكان من المعتدين باتمام ذلك الشاكرين الله عليه فما صنف في الإسلام قبله مثله ولا اتفق لأحد ما اتفق له، ومن قاس طريقته بطريقة المتقدمين في الأصول والفروع وأنصف أقر بعلو منصبه ووفور تعبه ونصبه، في الدين وكثرة سهره في استنباط الغوامض وتحقيق المسائل وترتيب الدلائل
The students and a group of imams, eminent scholars, and sons of dignitaries graduated under him, until they reached the level of teaching in his time. His attention to knowledge, his persistence in teaching, debating, and research organized means, assemblies, gatherings, and diligence in seeking knowledge—a thriving market for its people unknown before him. There was attached to him what befits his position of acceptance by the sultan, the vizier, and the pillars, and abundant respect from them such that no one else was mentioned. So he was the addressed, the pointed out, the accepted from him, the forsaken was the one he forsook, the reference in councils, those who attach themselves to his service, and the one looked to who drinks from his method in usul and furu'. Works were produced by him for the Nizamiyya court like al-Nizami and al-Ghiyathi, and their dispatch to the court, their acceptance, and their being met with appropriate gratitude and satisfaction, with excellent robes of honor, costly mounts, gifts, and grants. Similarly, he was entrusted with the leadership of the companions and the presidency of the group. The affairs of the endowments were delegated to him, and his dignity became the adornment of scholars, imams, and judges, and his word in fatwa was the reference of the great, the eminent, and the governors. He undertook a journey at the height of his days to Isfahan due to a conflict with some companions. He met there from the Nizamiyya council what was befitting his position of joy, honor, and respect with various kinds of kindness. He was given more than he sought and returned honored to Nishapur. His attention became mostly directed to composing the great work on the school called 'Nihayat al-Matlab fi Dirayat al-Madhhab' until he revised it and dictated it, and brought in it of research, estimation, refinement, investigation, verification, and realization what quenched the thirst, clarified the path, and indicated his rank and place in the science of Sharia. He taught the elite of students and finished it. Upon its completion, he held a session for the completion of the book attended by imams and the great, and he concluded the book in the manner of dictation and transcription. The group took delight in that, prayed for him, and praised him. He was among those who completed it, thanking God for it. No work like it was composed in Islam before him, nor was what happened for him attained by anyone. Whoever compares his method to the method of the earlier scholars in usul and furu' and is fair will acknowledge the loftiness of his station, the abundance of his toil and exertion in religion, and his frequent sleeplessness in deducing subtle points, verifying issues, and arranging proofs.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical description of a great scholar (likely Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni). It begins by noting that many students, including imams and dignitaries, graduated under him. His dedication to teaching and research created an unprecedented scholarly environment. The text then details his high status with the ruling authorities—he was the only one consulted and honored. He authored works for the Nizamiyya court, such as 'al-Nizami' and 'al-Ghiyathi', which were received with gratitude and gifts. He was given leadership over the companions and endowments. A journey to Isfahan due to a conflict with some companions resulted in great honor, and he returned to Nishapur. His main focus became the composition of his magnum opus, 'Nihayat al-Matlab fi Dirayat al-Madhhab', a comprehensive work on Shafi'i jurisprudence. He completed it with a special session attended by imams. The passage concludes by asserting the unmatched excellence of his work and his tireless effort in deducing nuanced points and arranging proofs.

Al-Bakharzi's Praise Through Comparisons
Al-Bakharzi's eulogy comparing the scholar to great imams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Bakharzi used comparative praise to elevate the scholar's stature among the great imams.

Core Idea
A scholar's excellence is measured by the company he keeps in praise.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's work quotes al-Bakharzi's eloquent eulogy. It is not a dry list of achievements but a rhetorical masterpiece that compares the scholar to the greatest imams. Understanding this helps us appreciate how medieval biographers used language to convey spiritual and intellectual rank.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Let the rhythmic prose and imagery sink in.
2
Identify the comparisons
Find each named imam and the quality for which the scholar is compared to them: jurisprudence (al-Shafi'i), literature (al-Asma'i), preaching (al-Hasan al-Basri).
Notice the pattern: 'So jurisprudence is the jurisprudence of al-Shafi'i, and literature is the literature of al-Asma'i...'
3
Examine the hyperbole
Look for phrases that amplify the scholar's stature: 'the imam of every imam', 'the victor over every lion'. Understand this as rhetorical convention, not literal claim.
Hyperbolic praise was common in medieval Arabic eulogies.
4
Reflect on the obscure final sentence
Consider the meaning of the last line about 'the school of hadith would have become a hadith'. This likely means the scholar's role preserved the tradition.
The exact phrasing is debated; the key is his indispensable role.
5
Consider the purpose
Ask yourself: why does al-Bakharzi use these comparisons? To establish the scholar's supreme rank and to inspire reverence in the reader.
This praise serves as a biographical monument within the larger work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولقد قرأت فصلاً ذكره علي بن الحسن بن أبي الطيب الباخرزي في كتاب ( دمية القصر ) مشتملا على حاله وهو فقد كان في عصر الشباب غير مستكمل ما عهدناه عليه من اتساق الأسباب وهو أن قال فتى الفتيان ومن اتجب به الفتيان ولم يخرج مثله المفتيان عنيت النعمان بن ثابت ومحمد بن إدريس، فالفقه فقه الشافعي والأدب أدب الأصمعي، وحسن بصره بالوعظ للحسن البصري وكيف ما هو فهو إمام كل إمام والمستعلى بهمته على كل همام والفائز بالظفر على أرغام كل ضرغام إذا تصدر للفقه فالمزني من مزنته قطره، وإذا تكلم فالأشعري من وفرته شعره وإذا خطب ألجم الفصحاء بغى شقاشقه الهادرة ولثم البلغاء بالصمت حقائقه البادرة ولولا سده مكان أبيه بسده الذي أفرغ على قطرة قطر تأبيه لأصبح مذهب الحديث حديثًا ولم يجد المستغيث منهم مغيثاً
And I read a passage mentioned by Ali ibn al-Hasan ibn Abi al-Tayyib al-Bakharzi in the book 'Damyat al-Qasr' containing his state, and he was in the time of youth not having completed what we have known him of the coherence of causes. He said: 'The youth of youths and one by whom youths are chosen, and the two imams (Abu Hanifa and Shafi'i) did not produce his like—I mean al-Nu'man ibn Thabit and Muhammad ibn Idris. So jurisprudence is the jurisprudence of al-Shafi'i, and literature is the literature of al-Asma'i, and his insight into preaching is that of al-Hasan al-Basri. And however he is, he is the imam of every imam, the one who rises with his ambition over every ambitious one, the victor with triumph over the spite of every lion. When he sits for jurisprudence, al-Muzani is from his raincloud a drop; when he speaks, al-Ash'ari is from his abundance a hair; when he delivers a sermon, he bridles the eloquent with the roar of his overflowing [speech] and silences the eloquent with the silence of his manifest truths. Were it not for his filling the place of his father with his filling that poured upon the drop of his [؟] reluctance, the school of hadith would have become a hadith, and the seeker of help would not have found a helper among them.'
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a quotation from al-Bakharzi's biographical work 'Damyat al-Qasr' praising the scholar. It uses a series of hyperbolic comparisons to establish his greatness: he is the best of youths, surpassing even the two great imams Abu Hanifa and al-Shafi'i. His jurisprudence is that of al-Shafi'i, his literature that of al-Asma'i, his preaching like al-Hasan al-Basri. He is the imam of all imams. When he teaches jurisprudence, even the great al-Muzani is but a drop from his cloud; when he speaks, al-Ash'ari is but a hair from his abundance. His sermons overpower eloquent speakers. The final sentence is obscure but suggests that without his filling his father's place, the school of hadith would have lost its way.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The passage claims the scholar is literally superior to the Prophet (peace be upon him).
Correction: The comparisons are limited to other human scholars and imams; such hyperbolic praise is a literary convention and does not extend to prophethood.

Al-Bakharzi's eulogy uses comparative rhetoric to place the scholar among the greatest imams, highlighting his excellence in jurisprudence, literature, and preaching.

The Scholar's Teaching Sessions and Eloquence
Ibn Asakir enumerates the scholar's teaching sessions and expresses regret.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the diverse teaching activities of the scholar as observed by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
The scholar's teaching encompassed eloquence, debate, public preaching, and high-level discussion.

Ibn Asakir describes firsthand the scholar's remarkable teaching sessions. From eloquent discourses to deep debates and emotional preaching, the scholar excelled in every format. This passage highlights the range and depth of his scholarly activities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to understand the flow.
Notice the repetition of 'كم من' which introduces four types of sessions.
2
Identify the four types of sessions
The passage lists four distinct types of scholarly gatherings. Find each one and note their characteristics.
They range from eloquent speeches to public preaching and high-level discussions.
3
Reflect on the emotional and intellectual mix
The preaching sessions combined jurisprudential gems, theological principles, and emotional elements like weeping and joy.
This shows the scholar's ability to engage both mind and heart.
4
Consider the narrator's regret
Ibn Asakir regrets not fully appreciating the scholar during his lifetime. Why might this be a common feeling?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو الحسن هذا وهو وحق الحق فوق ما ذكره وأعلى مما وصفه فكم من فصل مشتمل على العبارات الفصيحة العالية والنكت البديعة النادرة في المحافل منه سمعناه، وكم من مسائل في النظر شهدناه ورأينا منه إفحام الخصوم وعهدناه، وكم من مجلس في التذكير للعوام مسلسل المسائل مشحون بالنكت المستنبطة من مسائل الفقه مشتملة على حقائق الأصول مبكية في التحذير مفرحة في التبشير مختومة بالدعوات وفنون المناجاة حضرناه، وكم من مجمع للتدريس حاو للكبار من الأئمة ولقاء المسائل عليهم والمباحثة في غورها رأيناه، وحصلنا بعض ما أمكننا منه وعلقناه، ولم نقدر ما كنا فيه من نضرة أيامه وزرهرة شهوره وأعوامه حق قدره، ولم نشكر الله تعالى عليه حق شكره حتى فقدناه وسلبناه، وسمعته في أثناء كلام يقول أنا لا أنام لا آكل عادة وإنما أنام إذا غلبني النوم ليلاً كان أو نهارا واكل إذا اشتهيت الطعام أي وقت كان، كان لذته ولهوه وتنزهه في مذاكرة العلم وطلب من أي نوع كان، ولقد سمعت الشيخ أبا الحسن علي بن فضال بن علي المجاشعي النحوي القادم علينا سنة تسع وستين وأربعمائة يقول: وقد قبله الإمام فخر الإسلام وقابله بالاكرام وأخذ في قراءة النحو عليه والتلمذة
Abu al-Hasan said: This—and by the truth of truth, he is above what he mentioned and higher than what he described. How many sections containing eloquent high expressions and beautiful rare gems in gatherings did we hear from him? How many issues in discussion did we witness? And we saw from him the silencing of opponents and we have known that. How many sessions for reminding the common people, serial in issues, filled with gems derived from jurisprudential issues, containing realities of usul, making one weep in warning, making one joyful in glad tidings, concluded with supplications and various forms of intimate prayer—did we attend? How many teaching gatherings containing the great imams and the presentation of issues to them and discussion in their depths did we see? We obtained some of what we could from him and wrote it down. We did not fully appreciate the freshness of his days and the bloom of his months and years as they deserved, nor did we thank God for him as He deserved until we lost him and were deprived of him. I heard him during speech saying: 'I do not sleep, I do not eat habitually; I only sleep when sleep overcomes me, night or day, and I eat when I desire food, at any time.' His pleasure, amusement, and relaxation was in discussing knowledge and seeking it of any kind. And I heard Shaykh Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Faddal ibn Ali al-Mujashi'i al-Nahwi, who came to us in the year 469 AH, saying: 'And Imam Fakhr al-Islam accepted him and received him with honor, and he began reading grammar with him and studying.'
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is the narrator's (likely Ibn Asakir's) personal commentary after quoting al-Bakharzi. He affirms that the scholar's actual excellence surpasses even that hyperbolic description. He then lists the types of scholarly sessions he witnessed: eloquent discourses, public preaching sessions that combined jurisprudence and usul with emotional impact, and high-level teaching gatherings with leading imams. The narrator regrets not fully appreciating the scholar's lifetime. He then recalls a personal remark from the scholar about his habits: he does not sleep or eat by routine, but only sleeps when overcome and eats when hungry, regardless of time. His only delight was discussing and seeking knowledge. The passage ends with a report from a grammarian who studied with the scholar, confirming his acceptance and honor.

Key Terms
إفحام الخصوم
فصل
مجلس
مجمع للتدريس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir witnessed the scholar's multifaceted teaching, ranging from eloquent public addresses to deep scholarly debates, and regretted not cherishing it enough.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Scholar's Personal Habits and Devotion to Knowledge
Ibn Asakir recounts the scholar's personal habits and a grammarian's testimony.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
The scholar lived without routine, sleeping and eating only when necessary; his only delight was knowledge.

After describing the scholar's teaching, Ibn Asakir shares personal observations of his ascetic habits. The scholar's life was unbound by convention, and his ultimate joy was discussing and seeking knowledge. A grammarian's account confirms the scholar's generous reception of students.

Al-Bakhrizi's Poetic Praise of the Imam
Al-Bakhrizi's poetic eulogy for the Imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how classical scholars used poetic hyperbole to praise an Imam and what comparisons reveal about the Imam's stature across multiple disciplines.

Core Idea
Poetic praise elevates the Imam above all other imams in every field.

This passage from al-Bakhrizi's Damiyat al-Qasr offers a lavish poetic tribute to the subject of Ibn 'Asakir's biography. The panegyric uses exaggerated comparisons to establish the Imam's supremacy in fiqh, adab, wa'z, and oratory. We'll explore how such praise functioned in classical Islamic scholarship and what it reveals about the author's reverence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then review the translation. Let the poetic rhythm and hyperbolic style sink in before you interpret.
Notice the series of comparisons that structure the praise.
2
Identify the figures compared
List the earlier scholars to whom the Imam is compared: Abu Hanifa, al-Shafi'i, al-Asma'i, al-Hasan al-Basri, al-Muzani, al-Ash'ari. Reflect on the significance of each comparison.
These are major figures in fiqh, adab, wa'z, and kalam.
3
Understand the rhetorical purpose
Ask yourself whether the praise is meant literally or as hyperbole. The common misunderstanding warns against taking it as a literal claim of superiority over the earlier imams.
Such panegyric was a recognized genre with its own conventions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولقد قرأت فصلاً ذكره على بن الحسن بن أبي الطيب الباخرزي في كتاب ) دمية القصر ) مشتملا على حاله وهو فقد كان في عصر الشباب غير مستكمل ما عهدناه عليه من اتساق الأسباب وهو أن قال فتى الفتيان ومن اتجب به الفتيان ولم يخرج مثله المفتيان عنيت النعمان بن ثابت . ومحمد بن أدريس ، فالفقه فقه الشافعي والأدب أدب الأصمعي ، وحسن بصره بالوعظ للحسن البصرى وكيف ما هو فهو إمام كل إمام والمستعلى بهمته على كل همام والفائز بالظفر على أرغام كل ضرغام إذا تصدر للفقه فالمزني من مزنته قطره ، وإذا تكلم فالاشعرى من وفرته شعره وإذا خطب ألجم الفصحاء بالغى شقاشقه الهادرة ولثم البلغاء بالصمت حقائقه البادرة ولولا سده مكان أبيه بسده الذى أفرغ على قطرة قطر تأبيه لأصبح مذهب الحديث حديثًا ولم يجد المستغيث منهم مغيثاً.
And I have read a section mentioned by Ali ibn al-Hasan ibn Abi al-Tayyib al-Bakhrizi in the book (Damiyat al-Qasr) containing his condition, and he was in his youth not having completed what we had witnessed of his harmonious circumstances, and he said: The youth of youths and the one by whom youths are chosen, and the two muftis did not produce the like of him—I mean al-Nu'man ibn Thabit and Muhammad ibn Idris. So jurisprudence is the jurisprudence of al-Shafi'i, and literature is the literature of al-Asma'i, and his insight in preaching is that of al-Hasan al-Basri. However he is, he is the imam of every imam, the one exalted by his ambition over every determined one, the one victorious over the noses of every lion. When he presides for jurisprudence, al-Muzani is from his cloud a drop; when he speaks, al-Ash'ari is from his abundance a hair; when he delivers a sermon, he silences the eloquent with the roar of his thundering eloquence and makes the eloquent kiss the dust of his brilliant truths. Were it not for his taking the place of his father in a station that poured over a drop that his father refused, the school of hadith would have become a novelty, and the seeker of help would have found no helper.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a quoted eulogy from al-Bakhrizi's work 'Damiyat al-Qasr', praising an unnamed Imam (the subject of the biography). The author begins by noting he read a section describing the Imam's state in his youth, before he had fully matured. The quote then praises the Imam as the foremost youth, chosen above others, and claims that even the two great muftis—Abu Hanifa (al-Nu'man ibn Thabit) and al-Shafi'i (Muhammad ibn Idris)—did not produce someone like him. This is hyperbolic praise. The quote continues by attributing to him the best of various disciplines: his fiqh is that of al-Shafi'i, his adab that of al-Asma'i, his wa'z (preaching) that of al-Hasan al-Basri. He is called the imam of every imam, exalted by his ambition. Specific comparisons are made: when he teaches fiqh, al-Muzani (a prominent Shafi'i) is but a drop from his cloud; when he speaks, al-Ash'ari (the theologian) is but a hair from his abundance. His sermons silence eloquent speakers with their force. The final line warns that were it not for his occupying his father's position, the 'madhhab of hadith' would have become something novel and the helpless would have no helper—implying his role in preserving orthodoxy.

دمية القصر
الباخرزي
النعمان بن ثابت
محمد بن إدريس
المزني
الاشعري
الحسن البصري
الأصمعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Imam is literally superior to Abu Hanifa, al-Shafi'i, al-Ash'ari, etc. in their respective fields.
Correction: The praise is hyperbolic, intended to elevate his status in his own time, not to claim literal superiority over the earlier imams in all respects.

Key Takeaway

The Author's Testimony of the Imam's Virtues
Ibn Asakir enumerates his firsthand experiences of the Imam's sessions and expresses regret at his loss.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir personally witnessed and described the multifaceted virtues of the Imam through various teaching and preaching sessions.

Core Idea
Ibn Asakir's firsthand account brings the Imam's virtues to life beyond secondhand praise.

In the previous passage, al-Bakhrizi offered high praise of the Imam. Now, Ibn Asakir adds his own testimony, drawing on what he personally witnessed. He describes the Imam's eloquent assemblies, debates with opponents, preaching sessions for the common people, and teaching gatherings with senior scholars. This lesson explores these firsthand observations and the author's sense of loss.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the literal translation. Let the rhythm of the author's descriptions sink in.
Pay attention to the repetition of 'كم من' – it signals a list of experiences.
2
Identify the types of sessions
The passage mentions several kinds of gatherings: eloquent assemblies, speculative debates, reminding sessions for the common people, and teaching gatherings for senior imams. Find each one in the text.
3
Notice the emotional tone and regret
The passage begins with praise but ends with a poignant regret at not appreciating the Imam's blessings until after his death. Observe the shift in tone.
The author says he 'did not appreciate its due measure' and thanks Allah late.
4
Consider the significance of firsthand testimony
Why does Ibn Asakir include his own witness here? How does it strengthen the biography? Think about the trustworthiness of personal experience in historical writing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو الحسن هذا وهو وحق الحق فوق ما ذكره وأعلى مما وصفه فكم من فصل مشتمل على العبارات الفصيحة العالية والنكت البديعة النادرة فى المحافل منه سمعناه ، وكم من مسائل في النظر شهدناه ورأينا منه إفحام الخصوم وعهدناه ، وكم من مجلس فى التذكير للعوام مسلسل المسائل مشحون بالنكت المستنبطة من مسائل الفقه مشتملة على حقائق الأصول مبكية في التحذير مفرحة في التبشير مختومة بالدعوات وفنون المناجاة حضرناه ، وكم من مجمع للتدريس حاو للكبار من الأئمة ولقاء المسائل عليهم والمباحثة في غورها رأيناه ، وحصلنا بعض ما أمكننا منه وعلقناه ، ولم نقدر ما كنا فيه من نضرة أيامه وزرهرة شهوره وأعوامه حق قدره ، ولم نشكر الله تعالى عليه حق شكره حتى فقدناه وسلبناه.
Abu al-Hasan said: This—and by the truth of truth he is above what he mentioned and higher than what he described. How many a section containing eloquent high phrases and rare wonderful subtleties in assemblies we heard from him; how many a speculative problem we witnessed and saw him refuting opponents; how many a reminding session for the common people, serial in problems, filled with subtleties derived from fiqh problems, containing realities of usul, causing weeping in warning, causing joy in glad tidings, sealed with supplications and arts of intimate prayer we attended; how many a teaching gathering containing the senior imams and the presentation of problems to them and discussion of their depths we saw; and we acquired some of what we could from him and recorded it; and we did not appreciate what we were in, of the freshness of his days and the bloom of his months and years, its due measure; and we did not thank Allah Almighty for it due thanks until we lost him and were stripped of him.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is the author's own commentary following the quoted praise from al-Bakhrizi. Ibn Asakir asserts that the Imam is even greater than al-Bakhrizi described. He then enumerates various aspects of the Imam's activities he personally witnessed: eloquent speech in assemblies (fusul), debates in speculative theology (nazar), refutation of opponents (ifham al-khusum), preaching sessions for the common people that combined fiqh-derived subtleties, usul al-fiqh, emotional warnings and joyful tidings, all ending with prayers. Also teaching gatherings with senior imams. He collected some of his teachings but regrets not fully appreciating his blessings until after his death. The tone is one of loss and gratitude.

إفحام الخصوم
التذكير للعوام
مسائل الفقه
حقائق الأصول
فنون المناجاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author is criticizing or undermining al-Bakhrizi's praise.
Correction: Actually, Ibn Asakir affirms it and adds his own higher estimation, saying the Imam is 'above what he mentioned and higher than what he described.'

Checkpoint

A) Only fiqh lessons
B) Only theological debates
C) Reminding sessions for the common people that included subtleties from fiqh and usul
D) Only poetry recitals

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir's personal witness elevates the biography, showing the Imam's impact on both scholars and common people through eloquent speech, debate, preaching, and teaching.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What specific blessings from Allah—like a teacher, a study circle, or a spiritual gathering—are you currently taking for granted? How would you feel if you lost them today? What one action can you take this week to truly appreciate and thank Allah for that blessing?
?
Ibn Asakir witnessed the Imam's sessions but admits he did not fully appreciate them until they were gone. Is there a person (a parent, a scholar, a friend) whose presence you undervalue? What would it take for you to express gratitude to them before it's too late?
?
If you were to die today, would the people who benefited from you say they lost a blessing? Or are you living in a way that others will only realize your value after you're gone? Write down one change you can make starting tomorrow to be a greater source of benefit.
